كتاب النكاح باب المهر أو خمر أو خنزير أو على هذا الخل فإذا هو خمر أو على هذا العبد فإذا هو حر يجب مهر فائدته
إبلي هذه قال أبو حنيفة لها مهر مثلها وقال أبو يوسف : يعطيها ناقة من إبله ما شاء ا هـ . فإن الناقة كالعبد فينبغي أن تصح التسمية كما لا يخفى. وذكر في البدائع الجمل مع العبد وأنه تصح تسميته، ولا فرق بين الجمل والناقة إلا أن يقال إنها مجهولة ولا يمكن إيجاب الوسط مع التقييد بقوله من إبلي هذه فالمفسد للتسمية قوله من إبلي لا مطلق ذكر الناقة، ويدل عليه ما في المعراج أنه لو تزوجها على ناقة من هذه الإبل بل وجب مهر المثل فالإشارة والإضافة فيه سواء، وإن لم يكن المشار إليه في ملكه فلها المطالبة بشرائه، فإن عجز عن شرائه لزمه قيمته . وحاصله أن العرض المعين والمثلي كذلك تملكه المرأة قبل القبض لتعينه إلا النقدين فلا تملكه إلا بالقبض، وكذا غير المعين من الأولين. ومن أحكام العرض المهر أنه يثبت فيه خيار رؤية لأن فسخ العقد بالرد وهو لا يقبله، وأما خيار العيب فإن كان العيب يسيراً فلا ترده به ، وإن كان فاحشاً فلها رده هكذا أطلقه كثير واستثنى في فتاوى قاضيخان المكيل والموزون فإنها ترده باليسير والفاحش وفي المبسوط : كل عيب ينقص من المالية مقدار ما لا يدخل : تحت تقويم المقومين في الأسواق فهو فاحش، وإن كان ينقص بقدر ما يدخل بين تقويم المتقومين فهو يسير ا هـ. وقيد المصنف بالفرس ونحوه لأنه لو تزوجها على قيمة هذا الفرس أو على قيمة هذا العبد وجب مهر المثل لأنه سمى مجهول الجنس. كذا في الخانية. ففرق بين القيمة ابتداء وبقاء لأنه يتسامح في البقاء ما لا يتسامح في الابتداء. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو تزوجها على أربعمائة دينار على أن يعطيها بكل مائة خادماً فإنه يجوز الشرط ولها أربع من الخدم الأوساط . كما في الخانية بالأولى. وإن عين الخدم في هذه المسألة فهو صحيح . كما في الخانية بالأولى .

قوله : (وعلى ثوب أو خمر أو خنزير أو على هذا الخل فإذا هو خمر أو على هذا العبد فإذا هو حر يجب مهر المثل) بيان لثلاثة مسائل الحكم فيها واحد وهو وجوب مهر المثل لفساد التسمية الأولى إذا كان المسمى مجهول الجنس كالثوب لأن الأثواب أجناس شتى كالحيوان والدابة فليس البعض أولى من البعض بالإرادة فصارت الجهالة فاحشة. وقد فسر في غاية البيان الجنس بالنوع ولا حاجة إليه لأن الجنس عند الفقهاء وهو المقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالأحكام كإنسان والنوع هو المقول على كثيرين متفقين بالأحكام كرجل، ولا شك أن الثوب تحته الكتان والقطن والحرير والأحكام مختلفة، فإن الثوب الحرير لا يحل لبسه وغيره يحل فهو جنس عندهم وكذا الحيوان تحته الفرس والحمار وغيرهما، وأما الدار فتحتها ما يختلف اختلافاً فاحشاً بالبلدان والمحال والسعة والضيق وكثرة المرافق وقلتها فتكون هذه الجهالة أفحش من جهالة مهر المثل فمهر المثل أولى وهو الضابط هنا سواء كان مجهول الجنس أو مجهول النوع. وأما البيت فذكروا أن تسميته صحيحة كفرس وحمار، وقد بحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بأنه في عرفنا ليس خاصاً بما يبات فيه بل يقال لمجموع المنزل والدار فينبغي أن يجب بتسميته مهر المثل كالدار. وذكر في البدائع أنه لو تزوجها على بيت فلها بيت وسط مما وهو بيت الثوب لا البيت المبني فينصرف إلى فراش البيت في أهل الأمصار، وفي أهل البادية إلى بيت الشعر ا.هـ. وبه اندفع ما بحثه ابن الهمام لأنهم ما أرادوا به المبنى . وفي معراج الدراية : وفي عرفنا يراد بالبيت المبنى الذي من المدر يبات فيه فلا يصلح مهراً إذا لم يكن معيناً ا هـ . قيد بالثوب من غير بيان نوعه لأنه لو زاد عليه فقال هروي أو صحت التسمية ويجب الوسط أو قيمته ويخير الزوج كما قدمناه وكذا إذا بالغ في وصف الثوب في ظاهر الرواية لأنها ليست من ذوات الأمثال بدليل أنه لو استهلكها لا يضمن المثل. قال محمد وأصل هذا أن كل ما جاز السلم فيه فلها أن لا تأخذ إلا المسمى، وما لم يجز فيه السلم كان للزوج أن يعطيها القيمة والسلم في الثياب جائز إذا كانت مؤجلة ولا يجوز بدون الأجل فله أن يعطيها القيمة إلا في المكبل والموزون لها أن لا تأخذ القيمة وإن لم تكن مؤجلة لأن المكيل والموزون يصلح مهراً وثمناً من غير ذكر الأجل، أما الثوب الموصوف وإن صلح مهراً إلا أن الثوب يتعين بالتعيين فكان بمنزلة العبد ومن تزوج امرأة على عبد بغير عينه كان
Book of Marriage, Chapter of Mahr: 'or a garment, or wine, or a pig, or on this vinegar and it turns out to be wine, or on this slave and he turns out to be free - mahr al-mithl is obligatory.' Benefit: [If he says] 'one of my camels,' Abu Hanifa said: she gets mahr al-mithl; Abu Yusuf said: he gives her a she-camel from his camels, whichever he wishes. The she-camel is like the slave, so the specification should be valid as is not hidden. It is mentioned in al-Bada'i that the male camel and the slave are together and that specifying it is valid, and there is no difference between the male camel and the she-camel except that it is said she is unknown and it is impossible to mandate the middle with the restriction 'from these my camels.' So the invalidator of the specification is the phrase 'from my camels,' not the absolute mention of the she-camel. This is supported by what is in al-Mi'raj: if he marries her on a she-camel from these camels, rather mahr al-mithl is obligatory; so the pointing and the addition are the same in it. And if the pointed-to is not in his possession, she can demand its purchase, and if he cannot purchase it, he must pay its value. The conclusion is that a specified and fungible commodity is owned by the woman before possession due to its specification, except for the two moneys (gold and silver), which she does not own except by possession, and likewise unspecified commodities from the first two types. Among the rulings of a commodity as mahr is that the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) is established in it because the contract is rescinded by rejection, which it does not accept. As for the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), if the defect is minor, she does not return it; if it is major, she may return it. This is stated absolutely by many, except that in Fatawa Qadikhan, for measured or weighed items, she returns it whether minor or major. In al-Mabsut: every defect that decreases the value to an extent that is not within the assessment of valuers in the markets is major, and if it decreases to an extent that is within the assessment of valuers, it is minor. And the author restricted it to a horse and the like, because if he marries her on the value of this horse or the value of this slave, mahr al-mithl is obligatory because he named an unknown genus. Similarly in al-Khaniyah. So a distinction is made between value initially and subsequently, because there is tolerance in what remains that is not tolerated initially. And the author indicated that if he marries her on four hundred dinars on condition that he gives her for every hundred a servant, then the condition is valid and she gets four middle servants. As in al-Khaniyah preferably. And if he specifies the servants in this issue, it is valid. As in al-Khaniyah preferably. Then he says: 'And his statement: (And on a garment or wine or a pig or on this vinegar and it turns out to be wine, or on this slave and he turns out to be free - mahr al-mithl is obligatory) is an explanation of three issues whose ruling is one: the obligation of mahr al-mithl due to the invalidity of the specification. The first: if the named item is of unknown genus like a garment, because garments are various genera like animals and beasts, so some are not more deserving of intent than others, thus the ignorance becomes gross. In Ghayat al-Bayan, genus is interpreted as species, but there is no need for that because genus among jurists is that which is predicated on many different things in terms of rulings, like 'human', and species is that which is predicated on many agreeing in rulings, like 'man'. Without doubt, under 'garment' come linen, cotton, and silk, and their rulings differ; for a silk garment is not permissible for men to wear, while others are, so it is a genus for them. Similarly, under 'animal' come horse and donkey and others. As for a house, under it come things that differ grossly by region, location, size, spaciousness, and number of facilities; so this ignorance is grosser than ignorance of mahr al-mithl, so mahr al-mithl is more appropriate. This is the controlling principle here, whether it is unknown genus or unknown species. As for a 'bayt' (room/house), they mentioned that its specification is valid like a horse or donkey. The investigator Ibn al-Humam discussed that in our custom it is not specific to what one sleeps in; rather it is said for the entire dwelling and house, so specifying it should require mahr al-mithl like a house. It is mentioned in al-Bada'i that if he marries her on a 'bayt', she gets a middle 'bayt' which is the garment of the house (i.e., a cloth), not the building; so it refers to the bed covering in populated areas, and in desert areas to a tent. Thus what Ibn al-Humam discussed is refuted because they did not mean the building. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: in our custom, 'bayt' means the building made of mud in which one sleeps, so it is not suitable as mahr if unspecified. The author restricted it to a garment without specifying its type, because if he adds and says 'Harawi' (a type of cloth), the specification is valid and the middle or its value is obligatory, and the husband has the option as we presented. Similarly, if he exaggerates in describing the garment in the apparent narration because they are not of the type of fungibles, evidenced by the fact that if he consumes it, he does not guarantee the like. Muhammad said: the basis of this is that everything in which salam is permissible, she can only take the specified item; and what is not permissible in salam, the husband can give the value. Salam in garments is permissible if deferred, and not permissible without deferred time, so he can give the value. Except for measured and weighed items, she can refuse the value even if not deferred, because measured and weighed items are suitable as mahr and price without mentioning deferred time. As for the described garment, although it is suitable as mahr, the garment is specified by specification, so it is like a slave. And whoever marries a woman on a slave without specification...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explaining cases where the mahr (dower) specification is invalid due to defect or ambiguity, leading to the obligation of mahr al-mithl (dower of the like). The author begins by summarizing three scenarios: (1) mahr is a garment without specifying type, (2) mahr is wine or pig (impermissible items), (3) mahr is vinegar but turns out to be wine, or a slave but turns out free. In all these, the specification is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib. Then he addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the husband says 'one of my camels' (nabli hadhihi), Abu Hanifa rules mahr al-mithl because the phrase 'from my camels' makes it unknown which camel, so mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf says he gives any she-camel he chooses from his herd; the specification is valid because the she-camel is like the slave (specified by the herd). The commentary favors Abu Yusuf's view in terms of analogy but notes that the majority hold Abu Hanifa's view as per the base text. Then the author discusses general rulings for specified commodities (a'rad) as mahr, including khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection) and khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), distinguishing between major and minor defects. For measured/weighed items, the rule is different: even a minor defect allows return per Fatawa Qadikhan. The passage also covers the distinction between naming a value (qimah) versus an item, and the ruling on conditional employment of servants. The commentary then delves into the linguistic-legal distinction between jins (genus) and naw' (species), arguing that 'garment' is a genus under which various types with different rulings fall, so its specification without type is gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah) requiring mahr al-mithl. For a 'dar' (house), the ignorance is even grosser due to multiple variables, so mahr al-mithl is first. For 'bayt', there is a split: some say it is valid (like horse/donkey) but Ibn al-Humam challenges that in modern custom 'bayt' means a building, so it should be mahr al-mithl. The commentary resolves this by citing al-Bada'i that 'bayt' in this context means a cloth (thawb al-bayt) or tent, not a building, thus the earlier ruling stands. Finally, it discusses that if the garment is described with a type (e.g., Harawi), the specification is valid and the husband has the option to give the described item or its value, following the principle of salam (advance sale). For measured/weighed items, the rule is stricter: she can demand the same item, not value.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of the like: the amount typically given to women of the bride's status in her family and community.
الجهالة الفاحشة (al-jahalah al-fahishah): Gross ignorance: uncertainty about an essential aspect of the mahr that renders the specification invalid.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect: the right to return a defective mahr item and demand mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband marries a woman on the condition that she receives 'one of my camels,' what is the ruling of Abu Hanifa?
A) The specification is valid, and the husband gives one camel of his choice.
B) The specification is invalid, and she receives mahr al-mithl.
C) She receives the middle camel from his herd.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
When mahr is specified ambiguously (e.g., 'one of my camels'), the dominant Hanafi position is that the specification is invalid and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib; Abu Yusuf's contrary view is not relied upon for fatwa.

6 min
Invalidity of Specifying Dower by Genus Alone
Explaining that specifying dower by genus without further description leads to invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dower specified only by genus and explain why it necessitates mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
Specifying dower by genus alone is invalid—the excessive jahala triggers mahr al-mithl.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq: when a man specifies a dower (mahr) using only a general category (jins) like ‘a garment’ without further description, the specification is void due to excessive ambiguity (jahala fahisha). As a result, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl, the proper dower of women similar to her. The text defines jins and naw’, applies the rule to various examples, and addresses a nuanced disagreement about the word ‘bayt’ (room/house).

Guided Path
1
Distinguish jins and naw'
Identify the Hanafi definitions: jins is a category covering different realities with different rulings (e.g., ‘thawb’ includes silk, cotton, linen); naw’ is a more specific subset (e.g., ‘rajul’ under ‘insan’). This distinction is the foundation for measuring jahala.
2
Understand why jins alone creates excessive jahala
Because a single jins like ‘thawb’ includes items of vastly different value (silk vs. cotton), specifying only the jins leaves the exact mahr unknown. This jahala is considered fahisha (egregious), making the dower invalid.
Compare with specifying a specific type (naw’) or a specific item, which reduces jahala to an acceptable level.
3
Apply the rule to other examples
The text extends the same reasoning to ‘dar’ (house) due to extreme variation by location and size, and contrasts it with ‘bayt’ (room), which early scholars considered valid despite partial jahala.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'bayt'
Ibn al-Humam challenged the earlier ruling, arguing that in common custom ‘bayt’ can mean the entire house, so it should be treated like ‘dar’. The author defends the earlier view by citing al-Bada’i‘: ‘bayt’ in this context means a household cloth or tent, not a built structure, so its jahala is less.
This reveals how custom (urf) interacts with legal classification and the importance of understanding the terminology used by jurists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجهز به النساء، بالأحكام كإنسان والنوع هو المقول على كثيرين متفقين بالأحكام كرجل، ولا شك أن الثوب تحته الكتان والقطن والحرير والأحكام مختلفة، فإن الثوب الحرير لا يحل لبسه وغيره يحل فهو جنس عندهم وكذا الحيوان تحته الفرس والحمار وغيرهما، وأما الدار فتحتها ما يختلف اختلافاً فاحشاً بالبلدان والمحال والسعة والضيق وكثرة المرافق وقلتها فتكون هذه الجهالة أفحش من جهالة مهر المثل فمهر المثل أولى وهو الضابط هنا سواء كان مجهول الجنس أو مجهول النوع. وأما البيت فذكروا أن تسميته صحيحة كفرس وحمار، وقد بحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بأنه في عرفنا ليس خاصاً بما يبات فيه بل يقال لمجموع المنزل والدار فينبغي أن يجب بتسميته مهر المثل كالدار. وذكر في البدائع أنه لو تزوجها على بيت فلها بيت وسط مما وهو بيت الثوب لا البيت المبني فينصرف إلى فراش البيت في أهل الأمصار، وفي أهل البادية إلى بيت الشعر ا.هـ. وبه اندفع ما بحثه ابن الهمام لأنهم ما أرادوا به المبنى . وفي معراج الدراية : وفي عرفنا يراد بالبيت المبنى الذي من المدر يبات فيه فلا يصلح مهراً إذا لم يكن معيناً ا هـ . قوله (وبه اندفع ما بحثه ابن الهمام فيه أن ما ذكره عن البدائع لا يدفع ما بحثه من اختلاف الحكم باختلاف العرف نعم يدفع ما يشعر به كلامه من حمل كلامهم على أن المراد به ما يبات فيه فافهم
He furnishes with it women, with rulings like 'insan' and 'naw’' is said of many agreeing in rulings like 'rajul'. There is no doubt that 'thawb' includes linen, cotton, and silk, and rulings differ. For the silk garment is not permissible to wear, while others are permissible, so it is a genus (jins) according to them. Likewise animals include horse, donkey, and others. As for 'dar' (house), it includes what differs greatly by countries, locations, spaciousness/constriction, and many/few amenities, so this ignorance is more severe than the ignorance of mahr al-mithl, thus mahr al-mithl is preferable and this is the controlling rule here, whether the jins or the naw’ is unknown. As for 'bayt' (room), they mentioned that its specification is valid like a horse or donkey. The muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam investigated it, saying that in our custom it is not specific to what is slept in, but rather it is said for the entire house and dwelling, so it should necessitate mahr al-mithl like a house. It is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that if he marries her on a 'bayt', she gets a medium 'bayt', and that means a household cloth, not the built room, so it refers to a bedspread in cities, and in the desert to a tent of hair. End quote. And by this what Ibn al-Humam investigated is repelled, because they did not intend by it the built structure. And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: and in our custom 'bayt' means the built structure of clay that is slept in, so it is not valid as dower if unspecified. End quote. His statement: (And by it what Ibn al-Humam investigated is repelled) in it, that what he mentioned from al-Bada'i' does not repel what he investigated of the difference of ruling according to difference of custom; rather it repels what his statement suggests from carrying their words to mean what is slept in. Understand.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling of specifying a dower (mahr) that is ambiguous due to being described only by its general genus (jins) without further specification. The author begins by defining jins and naw’: jins is what encompasses various realities differing in rulings (e.g., ‘thawb’ includes silk which is forbidden, cotton and linen which are permissible), while naw’ is a more specific category within a jins, like ‘rajul’ under ‘insan’. The key point is that specifying the jins alone (like “thawb” without describing its type) causes excessive ignorance (jahala) because the value can vary dramatically. For example, a silk garment is haram for men to wear, while a cotton one is halal, so their values differ. This jahala is more severe than the jahala that necessitates mahr al-mithl (the proper dower). Therefore, the correct ruling is that such a specification is invalid, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl. This applies whether the jins or the naw’ is unknown. The text then extends this to ‘dar’ (house), which varies vastly by location and features, so its jahala is even more severe. As for ‘bayt’ (room), earlier Hanafi scholars considered it valid like a horse or donkey (which are valid despite jahala because they are specific entities). However, Ibn al-Humam argued that in common custom, ‘bayt’ does not specifically mean a sleeping room but can refer to the entire house, so it should be treated like ‘dar’ and invalidate the dower, necessitating mahr al-mithl. The author defends the earlier view by citing al-Bada’i‘: ‘bayt’ in this context refers to a household cloth (like a bedspread) in cities, or a tent of hair in the desert, not a built structure. Thus, its specification is valid because it is a known item. The margin note from al-Ramli clarifies that Ibn al-Humam’s objection is not fully refuted by this, because custom differs, but at least it shows the earlier scholars did not mean the built structure. In summary, when the dower is specified by a general genus without further description, the specification is void and mahr al-mithl is obligatory due to the excessive jahala. This is the controlling rule.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): A genus that encompasses multiple types differing in rulings, e.g., thawb (garment) includes silk, cotton, etc.
نوع (naw'): A species under a jins, e.g., raju under insan; in dower, specifying naw' reduces jahala.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equal to that of women similar to the wife, when the specified dower is invalid.
جهالة (jahala): Ignorance or ambiguity that renders a specification invalid if excessive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman on the dower 'a garment' (thawb) without specifying any type, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The dower is valid and she gets a garment of average quality.
B) The dower is invalid and she gets mahr al-mithl.
C) The dower is valid only if he specifies it as cotton.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A dower specified only by its genus is invalid due to excessive jahala, so the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.

Specifying Dower by Type or Measure: Husband's Option and Wife's Rights
Explaining the effect of specifying a type like Harawi or measurable items on the dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rules to determine whether a husband must deliver a specified dower item or may pay its value, and identify when a dower specification is void due to jahala.

Core Idea
When dower is specified by type, the husband may give the item or its value; only a precisely defined item must be delivered in kind.

In a marriage contract, the dower may be described by type (e.g., a Harawi garment) or by measure/weight (e.g., a sa'a of wheat). This lesson clarifies when the husband has the option to pay the value instead of delivering the specified item, and when the specification is void due to ambiguity, impacting the wife's entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the level of dower specification
Determine whether the dower is specified by genus only (e.g., 'a garment'), genus plus description (e.g., 'a good Harawi garment'), or a precise item (e.g., 'this specific slave').
2
Apply the rule for type-specified items
If the dower is specified by type and description (not a specific individual), the husband may choose to deliver the described item or pay its value. This is a concession to avoid hardship.
This is like the case of a Harawi garment described as 'good'.
3
Distinguish measured/weighed items
For makil or mawzun items (e.g., wheat, silver) where the genus and description are specified, the wife may demand the specific item. If unspecified, they are like generic commodities where value suffices.
Example: '10 sa'as of good-quality wheat' – wife can demand that specific wheat.
4
Handle void (laghw) specifications
If a dower includes an unspecified item alongside a known amount (e.g., 'ten dirhams and a garment' without description), the unspecified part is void, and only the known amount is valid dower.
Upon divorce before consummation, she gets half of the valid amount (5 dirhams) unless mut'a is greater.
5
Determine consequences of jahala (unknown quantity or genus)
If the dower is ambiguous in quantity or genus (e.g., 'dirhams' without number, or 'a house and servant' without description), the contract is valid but mahr al-mithl becomes due. If the ambiguity is partial and linked to a known portion, the ambiguous part is void.
Jahala of quantity is treated like jahala of genus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وكذا إذا بالغ في وصف الثوب قال الرملي : أي وكذا يتخير بين دفع الثوب أو قيمته ولو بالغ لا أنه يجب الوسط ولو بالغ فإنه إذا دفع الثوب اعتبر وصفه حتى لو قال ثوب هروي جيد له أن يعطي القيمة. كذا في الخانية. فالحاصل أن المكيل والموزون غير النقد إذا سمى جنسه وصفته صار كالمشار إليه العرض، وإن لم يسم صفته فهو كالفرس والحمار، وفي الخانية : لو تزوجها على عشرة دراهم وثوب ولم يصفه كان لها عشرة دراهم ولو طلقها قبل الدخول بها كان لها خمسة دراهم إلا أن تكون متعتها أكثر من ذلك اهـ. وبهذا علم أن وجوب مهر المثل فيما إذا سمى مجهول الجنس إنما هو فيما إذا لم يكن معه مسمى معلوم لكن ينبغي على هذا أن لا ينظر إلى المتعة أصلاً لأن المسمى هنا عشرة فقط وذكر الثوب لغو بدليل أنه لم يكمل لها مهر المثل قبل الطلاق وفي الظهيرية : لو تزوجها على دراهم كان لها مهر المثل ولا يشبه هذا الخلع ا هـ . وبهذا علم أن جهالة القدر كجهالة الجنس. وفي الخانية : لو تزوجها على أقل من ألف درهم ومهر مثلها ألفان كان لها ألف لم يصح لمكان الجهالة فصار كأنه تزوجها على ألف. وإن كان مهر مثلها أقل من عشرة قال محمد لها عشرة دراهم .اهـ. وفي البدائع لو تزوجها على بيت وخادم ووصف الوسط من كل واحد منهما ثم صالحت من ذلك زوجها على أقل من قيمة الوسط ستين ديناراً أو سبعين ديناراً جاز الصلح لأنه إسقاط للبعض ويجوز ذلك بالنقد والنسيئة، فإن صالحته على أكثر من قيمة الوسط فالفضل باطل لكون القيمة واجبة بالعقد.
His statement: (And likewise if he exaggerates in describing the garment) al-Ramli said: meaning he has the choice between paying the garment or its value even if he exaggerated; not that he must pay the average. For if he pays the garment, its description is considered, even if he said a good Harawi garment, he may give the value. Similarly in al-Khaniyya. The conclusion is that measured and weighed items other than currency, if he specifies their genus and description, become like a specific commodity; and if he does not specify a description, they are like a horse and donkey. In al-Khaniyya: if he marries her for ten dirhams and a garment without describing it, she gets ten dirhams; and if he divorces her before consummation, she gets five dirhams unless her mut'a is more. End. By this it is known that the obligation of mahr al-mithl when he specifies an unknown genus is only when there is no other specified dower with it; but according to this, one should not consider the mut'a at all because the specified here is only ten dirhams, and the mention of the garment is void, evidenced by the fact that he did not complete her mahr al-mithl before divorce. In al-Zahiriyya: if he marries her for dirhams, she gets mahr al-mithl, and this is not like khul'. End. By this it is known that jahala of quantity is like jahala of genus. In al-Khaniyya: if he marries her for less than a thousand dirhams and her mahr al-mithl is two thousand, she gets a thousand; it is not valid due to jahala, so it is as if he married her for a thousand. If her mahr al-mithl is less than ten, Muhammad said she gets ten dirhams. End. In al-Bada'i': if he marries her for a house and a servant, and describes the average of each, then she settles with her husband for less than the value of the average, sixty or seventy dinars, the settlement is valid because it is a remission of part; and it is permitted in cash or deferred. If she settles for more than the value of the average, the excess is void because the value is due by contract.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of dower specification. The author first addresses the scenario where the husband specifies a particular type of garment, such as "Harawi" cloth, even going into further description (like "jayed" or "good"). According to al-Ramli, the husband has a choice: he may either give the described garment (adhering to its description) or pay its value. If he gives the garment, he must fulfill the description; if he pays the value, he pays the value of a medium-quality item of that type. This is because such specified items are not considered "goods of the same kind" (dhawat al-amthal) that require replacement in kind; rather, they are like specific commodities. The text then distinguishes measured and weighed items (makil/mawzun) from non-currency items: if the husband specifies the genus and description of such items (e.g., "a sa'a of wheat of good quality"), they become like a specific commodity, so the wife may insist on receiving that specific item. If he does not specify the description, they are like a horse or donkey, where the husband may give the value because jahala is tolerated for specific items. The next part addresses a case where the dower includes a specific number of dirhams and a garment without description. Here, the garment specification is considered void (laghw) because it is ambiguous, and the valid dower is only the ten dirhams. If divorce occurs before consummation, she gets half of that (five dirhams) unless the mut'a (gift upon divorce) is more. This teaches that jahala of quantity (e.g., specifying a number like "dirhams" without amount? Actually the text says "on dirhams" meaning unspecified amount, which leads to mahr al-mithl) is similar to jahala of genus. Finally, the author discusses a case where the dower is a house and servant described as "average". If the wife later settles for less than the value of the average, it is valid because she is waiving part of her right. If she settles for more, the excess is void because the value is fixed by the contract.

Key Terms
تخيير (takhyir): The option given to the husband to either give the specified item or its value when dower is described by type.
مكيل وموزون (makil wa mawzun): Items sold by measure or weight, such as grains or metals, which have a different ruling in salam.
متعة (mut'a): A gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no dower is specified; here it is considered if greater than half the dower.
لغو (laghw): Void or legally ineffective; here, an unspecified dower component that does not affect the valid portion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ten dirhams and half the value of a garment.
B) Five dirhams unless mut'a is more.
C) Mahr al-mithl.
D) Ten dirhams only.

Key Takeaway
When dower is specified by type or measure, the husband may have the option to pay value or deliver the item; ambiguous parts may be rendered void, and jahala triggers mahr al-mithl.

10 min
Ruling on Specifying a Prohibited or Defective Dower
Explains invalidity of dower when prohibited or defective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when dower is specified as a prohibited item or turns out defective, and explain why the marriage remains valid while the dower specification is void.

Core Idea
Marriage with an invalid dower is valid; the wife gets mahr al-mithl.

In a marriage contract, the dower (mahr) must be something of legal value. If it is specified as something prohibited like wine or pork, or if the specified item turns out to be defective (e.g., a free slave), the specification is invalid. However, the marriage itself remains valid because a defective condition in marriage does not nullify the contract, unlike in sale. This lesson examines the Hanafi reasoning behind these rulings and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two sub-issues: (1) dower specified as an intrinsically prohibited item (muharram), and (2) dower specified as an apparently valid item that later proves defective or different.
2
Understand the concept of mal mutaqawwim
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between mal (wealth) and mal mutaqawwim (legally valuable wealth). Prohibited items like wine, pork, carrion, and blood are not mal mutaqawwim for Muslims, so they cannot serve as valid dower.
Carrion and blood are not wealth according to anyone, hence invalid a fortiori.
3
Apply the ruling – tasmiya invalid, marriage valid
When the dower is specified as a prohibited item, the specification is void, but the marriage contract is valid because the condition is fasid (defective) and does not affect the contract. The wife then receives mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers).
This is contrasted with a sale contract, where a fasid condition would invalidate the entire sale.
4
Note the exception for mixed dower
If the dower includes both a valid part (e.g., ten dirhams) and an invalid part (e.g., a liter of wine), only the invalid part is void; the valid part remains, and mahr al-mithl is not due. The wife gets the specified valid portion.
This is from al-Muhit.
5
Handle defective items
If the specified item appears valid but turns out to be defective (e.g., a slave who is free, a sheep that died, vinegar that became wine), the specification is invalid because the item is not deliverable as described. The wife gets mahr al-mithl.
When paying value, the husband must pay the value of the described quality (good, medium, or inferior).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية تسمية المحرم كما إذا تزوج مسلم مسلمة على خمر أو خنزير فإنه يبطل التسمية لأنه ليس بمال في حق المسلم كما في الهداية، أو مال غير متقوم كما في البدائع فوجب مهر المثل. وأشار إلى عدم صحتها على الميتة والدم بالأولى لأنه ليس بمال عند أحد أصلاً. وقيد في الهداية بأن يكون الزوج مسلماً، وقيد في البدائع بإسلامهما، والظاهر الأول أنه لو تزوج مسلم ذمية على خمر لم تصح التسمية لأنه لا يمكن إيجابها على المسلم. وقيد بكون المسمى هو المحرم فقط لأنه لو سمى لها عشرة دراهم ورطلاً من خمر فلها المسمى ولا يكمل مهر المثل. كذا في المحيط. وأشار المصنف إلى صحة النكاح لأن شرط قبول الخمر شرط فاسد فيصح النكاح ويلغو الشرط بخلاف البيع لأنه يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة المسألة الثالثة أن يسمي ما يصلح مهراً ويشير إلى ما لا يصلح مهراً كما إذا تزوجها على هذا العبد فإذا هو حر، أو على هذه الشاة الذكية فإذا هي ميتة أو على هذا الدن الخل فإذا هو خمر، فالتسمية فاسدة في جميع أو وسط أو، رديء اعتبر الوصف المعين إذا دفعه وكذا إذا دفع القيمة يدفع قيمة الجيد في تعيينه وقيمة الوسط في تعيينه وكذا الرديء قوله ( وبهذا علم الخ ) قال الرملي : تأمله. والذي يظهر أن الثوب لا يدخل في المهر ويحمل على التبرع به من الزوج قطعاً ولو دخل لكانت التسمية فاحشة معه فيوجب فسادها فيحمل على العدة كما جرت به العادة وعليك بالتأمل .اهـ. وجزم بهذا في فتاواه الخيرية وقال : وقد جعل في البحر تسمية الثوب لغواً وقد زاغ فهم صاحب البحر وأخيه صاحب البحر الرائق ج۳/ م١٩
The second issue: specifying a prohibited (muharram) item, such as when a Muslim marries a Muslim woman on wine or pork, for the specification is invalid because it is not wealth (mal) in relation to the Muslim, as in al-Hidaya, or it is non-valuable wealth (ghayr mutaqawwim) as in al-Bada'i', so mahr al-mithl is obligatory. He pointed to its invalidity for carrion and blood a fortiori, because it is not wealth according to anyone. It is restricted in al-Hidaya to the husband being Muslim, and in al-Bada'i' to both being Muslim. The apparent is the first, that if a Muslim marries a dhimmiya on wine, the specification is invalid because it cannot be imposed on the Muslim. It is restricted to the specified being the only prohibited item, because if he specifies for her ten dirhams and a liter of wine, she gets the specified (the dirhams) and mahr al-mithl is not completed. Thus in al-Muhit. The author pointed to the validity of the marriage because the condition of accepting wine is a fasid condition, so the marriage is valid and the condition is void, unlike sale which is invalidated by fasid conditions. The third issue: that he specifies what is valid as dower but points to what is not valid as dower, such as if he marries her on this slave then he is free, or on this slaughtered sheep then it is dead, or on this jar of vinegar then it is wine. So the specification is invalid in all. Or medium, or inferior, the specified description is considered if he pays it; likewise if he pays the value, he pays the value of the good in its determination and the value of the medium in its determination, and likewise the inferior. His statement (and by this it is known) al-Ramli said: reflect on it. What appears is that the garment does not enter into the mahr and is interpreted as a gift from the husband definitely; if it were included, the specification would be egregious with it, necessitating its invalidity, so it is interpreted as a gift as is customary. And you should reflect. End. And he affirmed this in his Fatawa al-Khayriyya and said: And al-Bahr made the specification of the garment void, but the understanding of the author of al-Bahr and his brother, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, deviated.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage covers two sub-issues. First, if the dower is specified as something intrinsically prohibited like wine or pork, the specification is void because these are not considered wealth (mal) for Muslims. Consequently, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl. The same applies to carrion and blood, which are not wealth at all. However, if the item is prohibited only due to a condition (like wine), the marriage itself remains valid because the condition is fasid (defective) and is waived, whereas in a sale such a condition would invalidate the contract. The specification of a prohibited item alone invalidates the dower, but if mixed with a valid dower (e.g., ten dirhams and a liter of wine), only the wine part is void and the dirhams are valid; mahr al-mithl does not become due. The second sub-issue involves cases where the specified item is apparently valid but turns out to be defective or different: e.g., a slave who is free, a sheep that is dead, or vinegar that is wine. In all such cases, the specification is invalid, and since the item is not deliverable, mahr al-mithl becomes due. The text also discusses the valuation when the husband pays the item or its value, and the margin note by al-Ramli clarifies that in some cases, an accompanying ambiguous item (like a garment) should be considered a gift rather than part of the dower to avoid excessive jahala.

Key Terms
محرم (muharram): An item that is not permissible to own or use, like wine, pork, carrion, blood.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Wealth that is legally valuable and permissible to use; prohibited items are not mutaqawwim.
تسمية (tasmiya): The specification of the dower in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim man marries a Muslim woman on a dower of a bottle of wine, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The marriage is invalid.
B) The dower specification is valid and she gets the wine.
C) The dower specification is invalid and she gets mahr al-mithl.
D) The marriage is valid and she gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
A marriage with a dower specified as a prohibited item or a defective item is valid; the dower specification is void and the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

6 min
Mahr with Unspecified Quantity or Quality
Rulings on mahr when specification is vague or missing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on mahr when the specified amount or type is unknown, and apply the Hanafi rule that jahalah invalidates the tasmia.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the mahr's type or quantity invalidates the specification, requiring mahr al-mithl.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on mahr specification. When the husband names a vague or undescribed mahr, the contract is not void, but the specified amount is considered invalid, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl—the proper dower of a woman of her status. This lesson explores the principles and specific cases that illustrate when a specification is valid and when it defaults to the proper dower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of mahr specification
Determine whether the mahr is specified by type (e.g., dirhams, cloth), quantity, and description. Note if any element is missing or vague.
If the mahr is a measurable or weighable item (makil/mawzun), it must be described; otherwise it is like an unspecified animal.
2
Assess validity of the specification
Apply the Hanafi rule: a valid specification (tasmia) requires knowledge (ma'lum) of type (jins), quantity (qadr), and quality (sifat). If any is unknown (jahalah), the specification is invalid.
Partial specification: mentioning an extra item without description is void (laghw).
3
Apply the consequence of invalidity
If the specification is invalid due to jahalah, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower). This replaces the invalid specified amount.
Exception: if there is a known specified mahr alongside the invalid part, that known mahr stands and the invalid part is disregarded.
4
Consider special cases from the text
Examine the cases: marriage for ten dirhams and an undescribed cloth (cloth void); marriage for less than a thousand when mahr al-mithl is higher (invalid specification, treated as if married for the stated lower amount); Muhammad's view on minimum of ten when mahr al-mithl is less than ten.
These cases illustrate how the principle is applied in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Nikah: Chapter of Mahr: He may give the value. Thus in al-Khaniyya. So the conclusion is that measurable and weighable items other than cash, if he specifies their type and description, become like a specific object (concept of a specific item). If he does not specify their description, then it is like a horse or donkey. And in al-Khaniyya: If he marries her for ten dirhams and a cloth, and he does not describe it, she gets ten dirhams. If he divorces her before consummation, she gets five dirhams unless her compensation (mut'a) is more than that. Dirham because the deficiency of the thousand... And by this it is known that the obligation of proper dower (mahr al-mithl) when he specifies an unknown type only applies when there is no known specified (mahr) with it. But according to this, one should not consider mut'a at all, because the specified (mahr) here is only ten, and mentioning the cloth is void (laghw) as evidence that he did not complete her proper dower before divorce. And in al-Zahiriyya: If he marries her for dirhams (unspecified), she gets proper dower, and this is not like khul'. And by this it is known that ignorance of quantity is like ignorance of type. And in al-Khaniyya: If he marries her for less than a thousand dirhams and her proper dower is two thousand, she gets a thousand; it is not valid due to ignorance, so it is as if he married her for a thousand. If her proper dower is less than ten, Muhammad said: She gets ten dirhams. And in al-Bada'i': If he marries her for a house and a servant, and he describes the medium of each, then she reconciles with her husband for less than the value of the medium, sixty dinars or seventy, the reconciliation is valid because it is a partial waiver, and it is permissible with cash and credit. If she reconciles for more than the value of the medium, the excess is void because the value is obligatory by the contract.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on mahr (dower) when the specification is vague or incomplete. It begins by stating that for items that are weighed or measured (makil/mawzun), if the husband specifies the type and quality, the ruling is like specifying a specific item (musharun ilayh). If he does not describe the quality, it is like specifying a horse or donkey (i.e., the husband must give a fair equivalent). Then from al-Khaniyya, a case: marriage for ten dirhams and an undescribed cloth — she gets only the ten dirhams; the cloth mention is void (laghw). If divorce before consummation, she gets half (five) unless mut'a (consolation gift) is greater. The passage then extracts the principle: the obligation of mahr al-mithl (proper dower) arises when the specified mahr is of unknown type (majhul al-jins) and there is no other valid specified mahr alongside it. Therefore, mut'a is not considered because the only valid specified amount is ten. Then from al-Zahiriyya: marriage for (unspecified) dirhams — she gets mahr al-mithl; this is not like khul' where specified compensation is valid even if unknown. Hence ignorance of quantity is analogous to ignorance of type. Then a case from al-Khaniyya: marriage for less than a thousand when proper dower is two thousand — she gets one thousand because the specification is invalid due to ignorance; it is treated as if married for one thousand. But if proper dower is less than ten, Imam Muhammad says she gets ten dirhams (the specified amount is validated). Finally, from al-Bada'i', a case where the husband describes a house and servant as medium, then wife settles for less — valid because it is partial waiver. If she settles for more, excess is void because the value (of the medium) is fixed by contract. This passage reaffirms Hanafi principles: specified mahr must be known (ma'lum) otherwise mahr al-mithl applies, and ignorance of quantity or type is treated similarly.

Key Terms
تسمية (tasmia): The specification of the mahr (dower) in the marriage contract, including type, quantity, and quality.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to that of women of similar status (family, beauty, etc.) to the bride.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the mahr's type or quantity that invalidates the specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman for ten dirhams and an undescribed cloth, then divorces her before consummation, what does she receive?
A) Ten dirhams and half the value of an average cloth
B) Five dirhams only, unless the mut'a is more
C) The value of an average cloth
D) Mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of the mahr's type or quantity invalidates the specification, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl, unless a valid known mahr coexists.

Invalid Mahr: Prohibited Items
Core ruling on invalid mahr specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when wine or pork is specified as mahr and explain why mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.

Core Idea
Specifying a prohibited item as mahr invalidates the specification, but the marriage remains valid and mahr al-mithl is due.

In a marriage contract, the mahr must consist of valuable property (mal mutaqawwim). What happens if the husband names a forbidden substance like wine or pork? The Hanafi school has clear guidance: the specification is void, but the marriage itself is not nullified. In this lesson, we explore the rule and its basis, including the a fortiori reasoning for dead meat and blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is specifying wine/pork as mahr. The ruling: the specification (tasmia) is batil (void) and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
The evidence: wine/pork are not mal mutaqawwim for Muslims.
2
Apply a fortiori reasoning
Dead meat and blood are even more emphatically invalid because they are not property for anyone.
The text uses 'first awla' (all the more reason).
3
Note the restriction on husband's religion
The ruling applies when the husband is Muslim, even if the wife is a dhimmi. If both are non-Muslim, the specification might be valid according to their own laws.
Al-Hidaya restricts to husband Muslim; al-Bada'i' requires both Muslim; the author prefers the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية تسمية المحرم كما إذا تزوج مسلم مسلمة على خمر أو خنزير فإنه يبطل التسمية لأنه ليس بمال في حق المسلم كما في الهداية، أو مال غير متقوم كما في البدائع فوجب مهر المثل. وأشار إلى عدم صحتها على الميتة والدم بالأولى لأنه ليس بمال عند أحد أصلاً. وقيد في الهداية بأن يكون الزوج مسلماً، وقيد في البدائع بإسلامهما، والظاهر الأول أنه لو تزوج مسلم ذمية على خمر لم تصح التسمية لأنه لا يمكن إيجابها على المسلم. وقيد بكون المسمى هو المحرم فقط لأنه لو سمى لها عشرة دراهم ورطلاً من خمر فلها المسمى ولا يكمل مهر المثل. كذا في المحيط. وأشار المصنف إلى صحة النكاح لأن شرط قبول الخمر شرط فاسد فيصح النكاح ويلغو الشرط بخلاف البيع لأنه يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة
The second issue: specification of what is prohibited (muharram). For example, if a Muslim marries a Muslim woman for wine or pork, then the specification is invalid because it is not property (mal) in the right of a Muslim, as in al-Hidaya, or it is non-valuable property (mal ghayr mutaqawwim) as in al-Bada'i', so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. And it indicated its invalidity for dead meat and blood a fortiori because it is not property at all for anyone. And it is restricted in al-Hidaya to the husband being Muslim, and in al-Bada'i' to both being Muslim, and the apparent is the first: that if a Muslim marries a dhimmī woman for wine, the specification is not valid because it is not possible to obligate it upon a Muslim. And it is restricted to the specified being only the prohibited item; because if he specifies for her ten dirhams and a pound of wine, she gets the specified (ten dirhams) and mahr al-mithl is not completed. Thus in al-Muhit. And the author (al-Marghinani) indicated the validity of the marriage because the condition of accepting wine is a void condition (shart fasid), so the marriage is valid and the condition is void, unlike sale because it is invalidated by void conditions.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage addresses the second mas'ala: specifying an item that is inherently prohibited (muharram) as mahr, such as wine or pork, in a marriage contract. The Hanafi ruling is that such a specification (tasmia) is invalid because wine and pork are not considered valid property (mal) for Muslims; they are either non-property or non-valuable property (mal ghayr mutaqawwim). Consequently, the husband must pay mahr al-mithl (the proper dower equivalent to that of women of similar status). The text draws a stronger analogy (first awla): if wine and pork are invalid, then dead meat and blood are even more so, as they are not considered property by any school. There is a restriction: the ruling depends on the husband being Muslim; if a Muslim marries a dhimmī woman (non-Muslim under Muslim state), the specification is still invalid because the husband cannot be obligated to pay wine. Another restriction: if the mahr includes both a valid item (e.g., ten dirhams) and a prohibited item (a pound of wine), only the valid part is valid; she gets the ten dirhams, and mahr al-mithl is not due (the invalid part is ignored). The marriage itself is valid because the condition (accepting wine) is a void condition (shart fasid); it does not void the contract, unlike in a sale (bay') where void conditions invalidate the contract. This highlights a key difference between marriage and sale in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
محرم (muharram): An item prohibited in Islam, such as wine, pork, dead meat, blood.
مال غير متقوم (mal ghayr mutaqawwim): Property that is not legally valuable; e.g., wine for Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim man marries a Muslim woman specifying a pound of wine as mahr, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid because the mahr is invalid
B) The mahr specification is void and she gets mahr al-mithl
C) She gets the wine if it is available
D) The husband must pay the value of the wine

Key Takeaway
Specifying a prohibited item as mahr does not invalidate the marriage; it voids the specification and triggers mahr al-mithl.

Mixed Mahr and Validity of Marriage vs. Sale
Extension to mixed mahr and comparison with sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for mixed mahr (valid + invalid items) and explain why void conditions invalidate sale but not marriage.

Core Idea
If mahr includes both valid and invalid items, only the valid portion stands; the marriage remains valid, unlike sale where void conditions invalidate the contract.

What happens when the mahr consists partly of a valid sum and partly of a prohibited item? The Hanafi school treats the valid part as the mahr, and the invalid part is ignored. Moreover, the validity of the marriage contract is preserved even if it includes a void condition, a significant departure from sales transactions. This lesson explores these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mixed mahr scenario
The case: the husband specifies 10 dirhams (valid) and a pound of wine (invalid) as mahr.
This is a mixed mahr where one component is invalid.
2
Apply the rule for mixed mahr
She receives the valid part (10 dirhams) and no mahr al-mithl is due.
The invalid part is simply void; the marriage is valid.
3
Understand the reasoning for void conditions in marriage vs. sale
A void condition (shart fasid) in marriage does not invalidate the marriage; it is void and ignored. In a sale contract, a void condition invalidates the entire sale.
This is because marriage is a stronger contract (aqd qawi) with greater flexibility.

Source Text

Three Hanafi Positions on Mahr When Pointed Item Differs
Intra-Hanafi dispute with reconciliation and principle extraction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on mahr when a pointed item differs from its description, and identify the underlying principle of genus (jins) that causes the disagreement.

Core Idea
When pointing and naming conflict in mahr, the genus of the item determines whether the naming or pointing prevails.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a husband specifies mahr by pointing to an item (e.g., 'this slave') that turns out to be fundamentally different (e.g., free)? Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani each offer distinct solutions. The key is their differing definitions of 'genus' (jins), which affects whether the pointing or the naming takes priority. Understanding this dispute reveals the sophistication of Hanafi usul and offers practical guidance for marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the case and identify the three positions
First, summarize the scenario: a husband specifies mahr by pointing to a specific item, but the item's true nature differs from its description. Then, state the three rulings: Abu Hanifa says mahr al-mithl; Abu Yusuf says pay the value of what was intended; Muhammad differentiates between essence errors and category errors.
2
Understand the unifying principle from al-Kafi
The passage presents a principle: when pointing and naming conflict, if the pointed-to is of a different genus than the named, the naming prevails; if same genus but different description, pointing prevails. Note that the dispute reduces to how each imam defines 'genus'.
3
Analyze each imam's definition of jins
Abu Yusuf defines genus by legal suitability (mal mutaqawwim vs. not). Muhammad defines genus by essence (dhat) and purpose (maqsad). Abu Hanifa defines genus by form (sura) and meaning (ma'na). Apply these definitions to the examples: free vs. slave, dead vs. slaughtered, vinegar vs. wine.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the woman gets mahr al-mithl (often more than the specified item's value); under Abu Yusuf, she gets the value of what was intended (usually the item's market price); under Muhammad, it varies by case.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text indicates that the relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's, as it is more practical. Fath al-Qadir prefers it. Conclude that in fatwa, the husband pays the value of the intended item (e.g., a medium slave).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة أن يسمي ما يصلح مهراً ويشير إلى ما لا يصلح مهراً كما إذا تزوجها على هذا العبد فإذا هو حر، أو على هذه الشاة الذكية فإذا هي ميتة أو على هذا الدن الخل فإذا هو خمر، فالتسمية فاسدة في جميع ذلك ولها مهر المثل في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي قول أبي يوسف تصح التسمية في الكل وعليه في الحر قيمة الحر لو كان عبداً، وفي الشاة قيمة الشاة لو كانت ذكية، وفي الخمر مثل ذلك من خل وسط، ومحمد فرق فوافق الإمام في الحر والميتة وأبا يوسف في الخمر. والتحقيق أنه لا خلاف بينهم وأن المعتبر المشار إليه إن كان المسمى من جنسه وإن كان من خلاف جنسه فالمسمى . قال المصنف في الكافي : إن هذه المسائل مبنية على أصل وهو أن الإشارة والتسمية إذا اجتمعتا والمشار إليه من خلاف جنس المسمى فالعبرة للتسمية لأنها تعرف الماهية والإشارة تعرف الصورة فكان اعتبار التسمية أولى لأن المعاني أحق بالاعتبار، وإن كان المشار إليه من جنس المسمى إلا أنهما اختلفا وصفاً فالعبرة للإشارة، والشأن في التخريج على هذا الأصل فأبو يوسف يقول الحر مع العبد والخل مع الخمر جنسان مختلفان في حق الصداق لأن أحدهما مال متقوم يصلح صداقاً، والآخر فالحكم حينئذ للمسمى وكأن الإشارة تبين وصفه ومحمد يقول : العبد مع الحر جنس واحد إذ معنى الذات لا يفرق، وأما الخل مع الخمر فجنسان أبو حنيفة يقول : لا تأخذ الذاتان حكم الجنسين إلا بتبدل الصورة والمعنى لأن كل موجود من الحوادث موجود بهما وصورة الخل والخمر والحر والعبد واحدة فاتحد الجنس فالعبرة للإشارة والمشار إليه غير صالح فوجب مهر المثل ا هـ . وارتضاه في فتح القدير وقال : وغاية الأمر أن يكون مسمى الخمر خلاً والحر عبداً تجوزاً، وذلك لا يمنع تعلق الحكم بالمراد كما لو قال لامرأته هذه الكلبة طالق، ولعبده هذا الحمار حر، تطلق ويعتق فظهر أن لا اختلاف بينهم في الأصل بل في اختلاف الجنس واتحاده، فلزم إنما ذكره في بعض شروح الفقه من أن الجنس عند الفقهاء المقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالأحكام إنما هو على قول أبي يوسف، وعند محمد المختلفين بالمقاصد، وعلى قول أبي حنيفة هو المقول على متحدي الصورة والمعنى . ثم لا يخفى أن اللائق كون الجواب على قول أبي يوسف وجوب القيمة أو عبد وسط لأن إلغاء الإشارة واعتبار المسمى يوجب كون الحاصل أنه تزوجها على عبد وحكمه ما قلنا .ا.هـ. وفي الأسرار أن أبا يوسف ومحمداً اعتبرا المعنى وأبو حنيفة اعتبر الصورة وآل الأمر إلى أن الذات الواحدة تلحق بجنسين إذا اختلفت صورة ومعنى والذاتان قد يلحقان بجنس واحد إذا اتفقا صورة ومعنى فلا ينسب غير أن إلى واحد إلا باتحاد الصورة والمعنى ولا الواحد إلى الغيرين إلا باختلاف الصورة والمعنى، وكلامنا في ذات واحدة لأن الوصفين اللذين اختلفا فيهما يتعاقبان على ذات واحدة على ما بيناه
The third issue: that he specifies something suitable as mahr and points to something not suitable as mahr, such as if he marries her on this slave but he is free, or on this slaughtered sheep but it is dead, or on this jug of vinegar but it is wine. So the specification is invalid in all of that, and she gets proper dower (mahr al-mithl) according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf, the specification is valid in all cases, and he must pay: for the free (man) the value of a slave if he were a slave; for the sheep the value of the sheep if it were slaughtered; and for the wine similarly (the value of) medium vinegar. And Muhammad differentiated: he agreed with the Imam (Abu Hanifa) regarding the free and the dead, and with Abu Yusuf regarding the wine. The verification is that there is no disagreement among them, and that what is considered is the pointed-to (musharun ilayh) if the specified (musamma) is of its genus, and if it is of a different genus, then the specified (is considered). The author in al-Kafi said: These issues are based on a principle: when pointing (ishara) and naming (tasmia) come together, and the pointed-to is of a different genus from the named, then consideration is given to the naming because it identifies the essence (mahiyya) while pointing identifies the image (sura). So consideration of naming is preferable because meanings are more deserving of consideration. If the pointed-to is of the same genus as the named but they differ in description, then consideration is given to pointing. And the matter in derivation upon this principle: Abu Yusuf says free and slave, vinegar and wine are two different genera with respect to dower because one is valuable property suitable as dower, the other is not. So the ruling then is for the named, and the pointing explains its description. Muhammad says: slave and free are one genus because the meaning of essence (dhat) does not differentiate, but vinegar and wine are two genera. Abu Hanifa says: the two essences do not take the ruling of two genera unless there is a change in form and meaning, because every existing thing exists by both, and the form of vinegar and wine, free and slave, is one, so the genus is one, so consideration is given to pointing, and the pointed-to is not suitable, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory. And it was approved in Fath al-Qadir, and he said: at most it can be said that the named wine is vinegar and free is a slave metaphorically, and that does not prevent attaching the ruling to the intended meaning, just as if he says to his wife: 'You are divorced' while pointing to a dog, or to his slave: 'You are free' while pointing to a donkey, she is divorced and he is freed. So it appears there is no difference among them in principle, but rather in the difference and unity of genus. Thus what is mentioned in some commentaries of fiqh that 'genus' (jins) according to jurists is said of many things differing in rulings, that is according to Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, it is those differing in purposes (maqasid); according to Abu Hanifa, it is said of things united in form and meaning. Then it is not hidden that the appropriate answer according to Abu Yusuf is the obligation of value or a medium slave, because cancelling the pointing and considering the naming entails that the result is that he married her on a slave, and its ruling is as we said. And in al-Asrar: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad considered meaning, while Abu Hanifa considered form. The matter reduces to that a single essence (dhat) may attach to two genera if form and meaning differ, and two essences may attach to one genus if form and meaning agree. So nothing is attributed to one except by unity of form and meaning, and one is not attributed to two except by difference of form and meaning. And our discussion is about a single essence because the two descriptions that they differ about alternate on a single essence, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the famous intra-Hanafi dispute on the third mas'ala: when the husband specifies a mahr by pointing to a specific item (e.g., 'this slave') but the item turns out not to be what it seems (e.g., the slave is actually free). The three positions are: Imam Abu Hanifa says the specification is entirely invalid, so mahr al-mithl is due. Imam Abu Yusuf says the specification is valid, and the husband must pay the value of what the item was supposed to be (e.g., value of a slave if it were a slave). Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differentiates: he agrees with Abu Hanifa when the error is in essence (e.g., free vs slave, dead vs slaughtered) because the genus changes, but agrees with Abu Yusuf when the error is in category (e.g., vinegar vs wine) because both are liquids and the genus is the same? Actually the text says Muhammad agreed with Abu Yusuf on the wine case, meaning he validates the specification and requires value of medium vinegar. The author then gives a unifying principle from al-Kafi: when pointing and naming conflict, if the pointed-to item is of a different genus than the named, the naming prevails; if same genus but different description, pointing prevails. The disagreement is about what constitutes different genera. Abu Yusuf: free and slave are different genera because one is mal mutaqawwim and the other is not; vinegar and wine are also different. Muhammad: free and slave are same genus (both humans), so pointing prevails (invalid), but vinegar and wine are different (one intoxicant, one not). Abu Hanifa: free and slave are same genus in form (both human form), and vinegar and wine are also same in form (both liquids), so pointing prevails in all, leading to mahr al-mithl. Fath al-Qadir and al-Asrar attempt to reconcile by metaphysical concepts of essence and form. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is likely Abu Yusuf's due to practicality. This lesson demonstrates the sophistication of Hanafi usul and the interplay of language (pointing vs naming) in legal determinations.

Key Terms
إشارة (ishara): Pointing to a specific item at the time of contract, e.g., 'this slave'.
مسمى (musamma): The named item (the verbal description in the contract), e.g., 'slave' even if not free.
جنس (jins): Genus; a category of things. The dispute hinges on how to define genus: by form, meaning, or purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a husband says 'I marry you on this slave' and the slave is actually free, what is the ruling?
A) The specification is valid and he pays the value of a slave
B) The specification is invalid and she gets mahr al-mithl
C) The specification is valid and he pays nothing extra
D) He must give the slave if he becomes free

Key Takeaway
This intra-Hanafi dispute turns on the definition of 'genus' (jins), and the relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's: the husband pays the value of the intended item.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Conflict Between Indication and Naming in Mahr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conflict between indication and naming in mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding mahr when indication and naming conflict, and apply the Hanafi principle of genus to determine the operative ruling.

Core Idea
If indication and naming conflict, the mahr depends on whether the two objects are of the same genus or different.

When a husband says 'I marry you on this' while naming something different, which mahr applies? The Hanafi school's three founding imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—gave different answers based on how they classified the genus of the indicated and named items. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
A man marries a woman, pointing to one object (e.g., a free person) but naming a different object (e.g., a slave). The marriage is valid, but the mahr amount is disputed.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf: value of the named item. Muhammad: follows Abu Hanifa for free person/dead animal, Abu Yusuf for wine/vinegar.
These positions are all recorded in zahir al-riwayah.
3
Analyze the underlying principle
The passage states: if indicated and named are different genera, naming governs; if same genus but different description, indication governs. The dispute is over what constitutes 'different genus'.
The definition of jins (genus) is not the technical logical genus; it's based on form (surah) and meaning (ma'na).
4
Apply the principle to examples
For free person vs slave: Abu Hanifa says they are same genus (both human form), so indication governs. Abu Yusuf says different genera (one is property, one is not), so naming governs. Muhammad splits between the two.
Similarly for wine (khamr) vs vinegar (khal): wine is not valuable property, vinegar is.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: wife receives either mahr al-mithl (Abu Hanifa) or the value of the named item (Abu Yusuf) or a mixed result (Muhammad). The mufta bihi is not explicit but Abu Hanifa's view is favored.
The wife may or may not be forced to accept a medium value item, depending on the view.
