Mahr al-Mithl in a Fasid Marriage: The Named Mahr Limit
Ruling on mahr al-mithl in fasid marriage with named mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr al-mithl in a fasid marriage and apply the rule that mahr al-mithl does not exceed the named mahr when it is known.

Core Idea
In a fasid marriage, mahr al-mithl is wajib but capped at the named mahr if one was agreed.

This lesson examines the delicate interaction between mahr al-mithl (fair dower) and mahr al-musamma (named dower) in a fasid marriage. The source passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that while a fasid contract invalidates the named mahr in principle, the wife's implicit consent to the named amount restricts any claim to mahr al-mithl beyond it. We will unpack the legal reasoning behind this rule and explore special cases, including the contested nature of marriage with a mahram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a fasid marriage where intercourse has occurred. The ruling is that mahr al-mithl is wajib (obligatory). This is stated at the beginning of the passage: 'المثل بالوطء' (the [mahr] al-mithl is by intercourse).
Mahr al-mithl is not due by the contract itself but by consummation in a fasid marriage.
2
Locate the key limit: the named mahr
The passage asserts that mahr al-mithl does not exceed the named mahr (ولم يزد على المسمى). The commentator explains this is because the wife did not name the increase, implying her consent to the named amount as a reduction.
This is the core talil (causal reasoning): the wife's silence on the increase is treated as waiver of any excess.
3
Apply the limit in both directions
If mahr al-mithl is greater than the named mahr, she gets only the named. If mahr al-mithl is less than the named, she gets only mahr al-mithl. The naming is considered invalid overall, but the consent to the named amount still binds her.
Exception: if the named mahr is unknown (majhul), then full mahr al-mithl is due, just as if no tie was named.
4
Consider the mahram marriage exception
In a marriage with a mahram (unmarriageable relative), Abu Hanifa holds it is batil; others say fasid. Regardless, mahr al-mithl is due in full, without any named mahr cap (since naming is even less relevant).
This shows the school's consistency: mahr al-mithl is always due when intercourse occurs in an invalid union, even if the contract is batil from the outset.
5
Note the minimum mahr comparison
In a valid marriage, mahr al-mithl has a minimum of ten dirhams. In a fasid marriage, if mahr al-mithl is less than ten, she gets that lesser amount, unlike the valid case.
This asymmetry underscores the weaker legal effect of a fasid contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثل بالوطء ولم يزد على المسمى ويثبت النسب والعدة ومهر مثلها يعتبر بقوم أبيها إذا مهر نصف قوله : (ولم يزد على المسمى) أي لم يزد مهر المثل على المسمى لأنها لم تسم الزيادة فكانت راضية للحط مسقطة حقها في الزيادة إلى تمامه حيث لم تسم : تمامه لا لأجل أن التسمية صحيحة من وجه لأن الحق أنها فاسدة من كل وجه لوقوعها في عقد فاسد، ولهذا لو كان المثل أقل من المسمى وجب مهر المثل فقط. وفي الظهيرية : ولو زوج أحد الموليين أمته ودخل بها الزوج فللآخر النقض، فإن نقض فله نصف مهر المثل وللمزوج الأقل من نصف مهر المثل ومن المسمى ا هـ . فعلى هذا يعطى هذا العقد حكم الفاسد بالنسبة إلى المزوج وحكم العدم بالنسبة إلى غيره. وأشار إلى أن المسمى معلوم ولذا لا يزاد عليه فلو كان المسمى مجهولا وجب مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ اتفاقاً كما إذا لم يكن فيه تسمية أصلاً، وظاهر كلامهم أن المثل لو كان أقل من مهر العشرة فليس لها إلا مهر المثل بخلاف النكاح الصحيح إذا وجب فيه مهر المثل فإنه لا ينقص عن عشرة. وفي الخانية : لو تزوج محرمه لأحد عليه في قول أبي حنيفة وعليه مهر مثلها بالغاً ما بلغ ا هـ . فإن كان النكاح باطلاً فظاهر، وإن كان فاسداً فهي مستثناة، وقد نقل الاختلاف في جامع الفصولين فقيل باطل عنده وسقوط الحد لشبهة الاشتباه، وقيل فاسد وسقطوه لشبهة
The [mahr] al-mithl is by intercourse, and it does not exceed the named [mahr], and lineage and waiting period are established, and her mahr al-mithl is considered by the value of her father's family if half the mahr... He said: (and it does not exceed the named) meaning mahr al-mithl does not exceed the named mahr because she did not name the increase, so she is considered satisfied with the reduction, dropping her right to the increase up to its completion since she did not name it: its completion, not because the naming is valid in some respect, for the correct view is that it is invalid in every respect because it occurs in an invalid contract. For this reason, if the mithl is less than the named, only mahr al-mithl is due. And in al-Zahiriya: If one of the two guardians marries his female slave and the husband enters her, the other has the right to annul. If he annuls, he gets half of mahr al-mithl, and the one who married gets the lesser of half of mahr al-mithl and the named mahr. So according to this, this contract is given the ruling of fasid with respect to the one who married, and the ruling of non-existence with respect to others. And he indicated that the named is known, so it is not increased. If the named is unknown, then full mahr al-mithl is due, according to agreement, as if there was no naming at all. And it appears from their statements that if the mithl is less than ten dirhams, she gets only mahr al-mithl, contrary to a valid marriage where mahr al-mithl is not less than ten. And in al-Khaniya: If he marries his mahram, there is nothing against him according to Abu Hanifa, and he owes her mahr al-mithl whatever it is. So if the marriage is batil, it is apparent; and if it is fasid, then it is excepted. The difference has been reported in Jami' al-Fusulayn: it was said that it is batil according to him, and the hadd is dropped due to the doubt of suspicion; and it was said it is fasid and they dropped it due to doubt...
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage deals with mahr al-mithl (fair dower) in a fasid (invalid) marriage. The matn states that mahr al-mithl is established by intercourse, but it does not exceed the named mahr (mahr musamma) if a mahr was named. The commentator explains that the wife is considered to have agreed to the named mahr dropping any increase, so mahr al-mithl is not given beyond it. However, if the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, she is restricted to the named; if it is more, she gets mahr al-mithl. The exception is when the named mahr is unknown, then full mahr al-mithl is due. The commentator also discusses a scenario from al-Zahiriya involving two guardians. Then he addresses the case of marriage with a mahram (unmarriageable relative): according to Abu Hanifa, the marriage is batil (or fasid) and the husband owes mahr al-mithl. The text ends with a citation of a difference of opinion about whether such a marriage is batil or fasid, but the mahr obligation remains.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The fair dower determined by the bride's circumstances (family status, age, beauty, etc.) when no mahr is named or the named mahr is invalid.
مهر المسمى (mahr al-musamma): The dower explicitly named in the marriage contract.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to blood relation, suckling, or affinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid marriage where a named mahr is known and less than mahr al-mithl, what amount is due?
A) Mahr al-mithl in full
B) The named mahr
C) Half of mahr al-mithl
D) Ten dirhams

Key Takeaway
In a fasid marriage, the wife's mahr al-mithl is wajib but capped by the named mahr if known, reflecting her presumed consent to that amount.

Mahr al-Mithl in Fasid Marriage: Limitation by Named Mahr
Ruling on mahr al-mithl limitation in fasid marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on mahr al-mithl in fasid marriage and apply the condition that it does not exceed the named mahr.

Core Idea
In fasid marriage, wife gets mahr al-mithl but not exceeding the named mahr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses a key question: what happens to the mahr when a fasid marriage is consummated? The answer involves both the equitable dower (mahr al-mithl) and the amount specified in the contract. The rule balances fairness with the wife's implied consent to the lesser amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a fasid marriage that has been consummated. The ruling is that the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the dower of women similar to her, e.g., her paternal relatives.
2
Understand the limitation
The mahr al-mithl cannot exceed the named mahr in the contract. If the named mahr is higher, she only gets mahr al-mithl. Reason: she implicitly consented to the lower amount by not naming it.
If the named mahr is unknown, she gets mahr al-mithl without limitation.
3
Examine the exception from al-Dhahiriyya
In case of a slave-girl married by one guardian and annulled by another, the annulling guardian gets half of mahr al-mithl, the marrying guardian gets the lesser of half of mahr al-mithl and the named mahr.
This treats the contract as fasid for the marrying guardian and non-existent for others.
4
Note the difference from valid marriage
In valid marriage, if mahr al-mithl is less than 10 dirhams, it is raised to 10 dirhams. In fasid marriage, the minimum is not enforced.
The fasid marriage rule does not have the 10-dirham floor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مهر المثل بالوطء ولم يزد على المسمى ويثبت النسب والعدة ومهر مثلها يعتبر بقوم أبيها إذا مهر نصف
قوله : (ولم يزد على المسمى) أي لم يزد مهر المثل على المسمى لأنها لم تسم الزيادة فكانت راضية للحط مسقطة حقها في الزيادة إلى تمامه حيث لم تسم : تمامه لا لأجل أن التسمية صحيحة من وجه لأن الحق أنها فاسدة من كل وجه لوقوعها في عقد فاسد، ولهذا لو كان المثل أقل من المسمى وجب مهر المثل فقط. وفي الظهيرية : ولو زوج أحد الموليين أمته ودخل بها الزوج فللآخر النقض، فإن نقض فله نصف مهر المثل وللمزوج الأقل من نصف مهر المثل ومن المسمى ا هـ . فعلى هذا يعطى هذا العقد حكم الفاسد بالنسبة إلى المزوج وحكم العدم بالنسبة إلى غيره. وأشار إلى أن المسمى معلوم ولذا لا يزاد عليه فلو كان المسمى مجهولا وجب مهر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ اتفاقاً كما إذا لم يكن فيه تسمية أصلاً، وظاهر كلامهم أن المثل لو كان أقل من مهر العشرة فليس لها إلا مهر المثل بخلاف النكاح الصحيح إذا وجب فيه مهر المثل فإنه لا ينقص عن عشرة. وفي الخانية : لو تزوج محرمه لأحد عليه في قول أبي حنيفة وعليه مهر مثلها بالغاً ما بلغ ا هـ . فإن كان النكاح باطلاً فظاهر، وإن كان فاسداً فهي مستثناة، وقد نقل الاختلاف في جامع الفصولين فقيل باطل عنده وسقوط الحد لشبهة الاشتباه، وقيل فاسد وسقطوه لشبهة
فاسدها وباطلها وصرحوا بأن الإقالة كالنكاح لا يبطلها الشرط الفاسد، وقد عرف أنه لا فرق بين فاسده وباطله وقالوا لو وقعت الإقالة بعد القبض بعدما ولدت الجارية فهي باطلة ا هـ . کلام النهر. ولم يتكلم على القسمة الفاسدة كالقسمة على شرط هبة أو صدقة أو بيع من المقسوم أو غيره، وفي متن التنوير : المقبوض بالقسمة الفاسدة يثبت الملك فيه ويفيد التصرف كالمقبوض بالشراء الفاسد وقيل لا ا هـ. وقد نظمت هذه الإحدى وعشرين بقولي :
جملة مـامـن الـعـقـود فـاســد عشرون صرحوا بها وواحد البيع والنكاح والمضاربه إجارة والرهن والمكاتبــه صلح وقرض هبة مزارعه عدتها نظماً لحفظ نافعه وخلع وكالة بسلم فـاسـتـمــعــوا وصية الصرف وإلا قاله وقسمة والوقف والكفاله

شركة
عقود أتت إحدى وعشرين قد ترى فواسد فاحفظها تكن ذا جلاله كذاهبة قرض وخلع وصية مزارعة صرف ووقف إقاله مضاربة بيع نكاح إجارة مكاتبة رهن وصلح كفاله كذا سلم مع شركة ثم قسمة كذا صدقات والـتـمـام الـوكـالـه
Mahr al-mithl by intercourse and does not exceed the named (mahr), and nasab and iddah are established, and her mahr al-mithl is considered by the value of her father’s clan when she has half of the mahr. His statement: (and does not exceed the named) i.e., mahr al-mithl does not exceed the named because she did not name the excess, so she is consenting to reduction, giving up her right to the excess to its completion, since she did not name it; its completion is not because the naming is valid in one respect, because the truth is that it is invalid from every respect due to its occurrence in an invalid contract. For this reason, if the mithl is less than the named, only mahr al-mithl is obligatory. And in al-Dhahiriyya: If one of the two guardians marries off his slave-girl and the husband consummates, the other guardian has the right to annul. If he annuls, he gets half of mahr al-mithl, and the one who married gets the lesser of half of mahr al-mithl and the named mahr. So according to this, this contract is given the ruling of fasid in relation to the marrying guardian, and the ruling of non-existence in relation to others. He indicated that the named is known, so it is not increased; if the named is unknown, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory, whatever it may be, by agreement, as if there was no naming at all. The apparent meaning of their words is that if the mithl is less than ten dirhams mahr, she only gets mahr al-mithl, unlike in a valid marriage when mahr al-mithl is obligatory, it is not less than ten. In al-Khaniyya: If one marries his mahram, there is (a ruling) according to Abu Hanifa, and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl whatever it may be. So if the marriage is batil, it is apparent; if it is fasid, then she is excepted. The difference has been transmitted in Jami‘ al-Fusulayn: it is said batil according to him and the hadd is dropped due to the doubt of confusion, and it is said fasid and they dropped it due to the doubt. Their fasid and batil, and they stated that iqala (rescission) like marriage is not invalidated by a fasid condition. It is known that there is no difference between its fasid and batil, and they said: if iqala occurs after possession after the slave-girl gave birth, it is batil. This is the speech of al-Nahr. He did not discuss the fasid division like division on condition of gift or charity or sale of the divided item or others. In Matn al-Tanwir: What is taken by fasid division confirms ownership and permits disposition like what is taken by fasid purchase, and it is said no. I have composed these twenty-one (fasid contracts) in my saying: The total of contracts that are fasid are twenty, they explicitly stated, and one: sale, marriage, mudaraba, ijarah, rahn, kitaba, sulh, loan, hibah, muzara‘a, their count in poetry for beneficial memorization, khul‘, agency, salam, listen, will, sarf, and (others) they said, and division, waqf, and kafala, charity. And I also said: Company, contracts numbering twenty-one you see as fasid, so memorize them and you will have dignity: like hibah, loan, khul‘, will, muzara‘a, sarf, waqf, iqala, mudaraba, sale, marriage, ijarah, kitaba, rahn, sulh, kafala, also salam with company, then division, and charities, and the completion is agency.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq, specifically on the chapter of mahr in the book of marriage. The passage begins by stating a ruling: in a fasid (invalid) marriage that is consummated, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the equitable dower), but this mahr al-mithl cannot exceed the amount named in the contract. If the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, she only gets the named amount because she implicitly consented to the reduction by not naming more. However, if the named mahr is unknown, she gets mahr al-mithl regardless. The commentary then clarifies that if mahr al-mithl is less than the named amount, she receives only mahr al-mithl. An exception from al-Dhahiriyya is cited: if one of two guardians marries a slave-girl and the other guardian annuls, the annulling guardian gets half of mahr al-mithl, while the marrying guardian gets the lesser of half of mahr al-mithl and the named mahr. This treats the contract as fasid for the marrying guardian and non-existent for others. The text also mentions that if the mahr al-mithl is less than ten dirhams, the wife only gets that, unlike valid marriage where mahr al-mithl is at least ten dirhams. There is a discussion about marrying a mahram, where according to Abu Hanifa, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, though there is disagreement on whether such a marriage is batil or fasid. The passage then lists twenty-one fasid contracts in poetic form: sale, marriage, mudaraba, ijarah, rahn, kitaba, sulh, loan, hibah, muzara‘a, khul‘, agency, salam, will, sarf, waqf, iqala, division, kafala, charity, and company. This enumeration is for easy memorization.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable dower determined by the dower of women similar to the bride in status, such as her paternal relatives.
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage contract that is defective in some condition but not fundamentally invalid; consummation triggers certain effects like mahr and nasab.
المسمى (al-musamma): The dower named in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid marriage where the named mahr is 200 dirhams and mahr al-mithl is 150 dirhams, how much mahr is the wife entitled to?
A) 200 dirhams
B) 150 dirhams
C) 350 dirhams
D) 100 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In fasid marriage, the wife receives mahr al-mithl but not exceeding the named mahr, unless the named mahr is unknown.

Twenty-One Fasid Contracts: A Mnemonic List
Poem listing 21 fasid contracts for memorization.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twenty-one contracts considered fasid in the Hanafi school and identify their common characteristic.

Core Idea
Hanafi fiqh enumerates 21 specific contracts as fasid to help jurists memorize and apply rulings.

This passage concludes with a poetic enumeration of twenty-one contracts that are fasid in the Hanafi school. The list serves as a mnemonic aid for students and jurists. Each contract has its own ruling regarding validity, but all share a defect that prevents them from being fully valid (sahih).

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the list
The list is provided as a mnemonic to help memorize the contracts that are considered fasid in Hanafi fiqh.
Knowing these contracts helps in identifying potential legal issues.
2
Read the poem carefully
The poem lists the contracts in two stanzas. Read it twice to note the sequence and any repetitions.
The first stanza gives 20 contracts, the second adds 1 more (company) and repeats some.
3
Note the types of contracts
Contracts include sales, marriage, partnerships, loans, gifts, etc. Observe that many are common transactions.
Fasid contracts are defective in conditions or pillars, not fundamentally invalid.

He did not discuss the fasid division like division on condition of gift or charity or sale of the divided item or others. In Matn al-Tanwir: What is taken by fasid division confirms ownership and permits disposition like what is taken by fasid purchase, and it is said no. I have composed these twenty-one (fasid contracts) in my saying: The total of contracts that are fasid are twenty, they explicitly stated, and one: sale, marriage, mudaraba, ijarah, rahn, kitaba, sulh, loan, hibah, muzara‘a, their count in poetry for beneficial memorization, khul‘, agency, salam, listen, will, sarf, and (others) they said, and division, waqf, and kafala, charity. And I also said: Company, contracts numbering twenty-one you see as fasid, so memorize them and you will have dignity: like hibah, loan, khul‘, will, muzara‘a, sarf, waqf, iqala, mudaraba, sale, marriage, ijarah, kitaba, rahn, sulh, kafala, also salam with company, then division, and charities, and the completion is agency.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq, specifically on the chapter of mahr in the book of marriage. The passage begins by stating a ruling: in a fasid (invalid) marriage that is consummated, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the equitable dower), but this mahr al-mithl cannot exceed the amount named in the contract. If the named mahr is less than mahr al-mithl, she only gets the named amount because she implicitly consented to the reduction by not naming more. However, if the named mahr is unknown, she gets mahr al-mithl regardless. The commentary then clarifies that if mahr al-mithl is less than the named amount, she receives only mahr al-mithl. An exception from al-Dhahiriyya is cited: if one of two guardians marries a slave-girl and the other guardian annuls, the annulling guardian gets half of mahr al-mithl, while the marrying guardian gets the lesser of half of mahr al-mithl and the named mahr. This treats the contract as fasid for the marrying guardian and non-existent for others. The text also mentions that if the mahr al-mithl is less than ten dirhams, the wife only gets that, unlike valid marriage where mahr al-mithl is at least ten dirhams. There is a discussion about marrying a mahram, where according to Abu Hanifa, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, though there is disagreement on whether such a marriage is batil or fasid. The passage then lists twenty-one fasid contracts in poetic form: sale, marriage, mudaraba, ijarah, rahn, kitaba, sulh, loan, hibah, muzara‘a, khul‘, agency, salam, will, sarf, waqf, iqala, division, kafala, charity, and company. This enumeration is for easy memorization.

Key Terms
العقد الفاسد (al-‘aqd al-fasid): A contract that is defective in some condition or pillar but not fundamentally invalid; effects may still occur upon execution.
النظم (al-nazm): Poetic composition used as a mnemonic device for memorizing legal lists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many fasid contracts are listed in total according to the poem?
A) 20
B) 21
C) 22
D) 19

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school identifies 21 specific contracts as fasid, useful for memorization and applying corrective rulings.

Nikah — Marriage

Establishing Lineage in a Fasid Marriage: The Dispute over the Start of the Period
Intra-Hanafi dispute on period start for lineage in fasid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi position regarding the start of the six-month period for establishing lineage in a fasid marriage and explain the istihsan reasoning that sets it apart from the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
In a fasid marriage, the six-month period for lineage starts from consummation, not the contract, because the marriage does not encourage intercourse.

This passage dives into a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about when the clock starts ticking for a child's lineage in a defective (fasid) marriage. The majority view led by Imam Muhammad relies on istihsan, considering the unique nature of a fasid marriage, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize to a valid marriage. The difference has real consequences for paternity and inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The issue is the starting point of the six-month period that must pass after the earliest possible intercourse for a child to be attributed to the husband in a fasid marriage.
In a valid marriage, the period starts from the contract by consensus.
2
State each position and its evidence
Imam Muhammad: period starts from consummation (dukhul) because a fasid marriage does not motivate intercourse. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: from the contract, analogizing to a valid marriage.
The differing positions are all within the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Imam Muhammad's view is based on istihsan: the 'illa (effective cause) for starting from consummation is that the fasid marriage lacks the incentive for intercourse, so mere contract is not sufficient evidence.
The opposing analogy is rejected because the basis (valid marriage) is not comparable.
4
Apply the practical consequence
If a child is born six months after the contract but less than six months after consummation, lineage is not established according to the mufta bihi view.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
5
Distinguish fasid from batil
The passage also discusses the distinction between fasid (defective) and batil (void) marriages, noting that the marriage of mahrams may be batil, affecting hadd punishment.
This distinction is important for other rulings like 'idda and lineage.

His statement: 'Because the aforementioned analogy is not valid' because the fasid marriage does not prompt to intercourse due to its prohibition, hence the prohibition of in-laws is not established by mere contract without intercourse or touching or kissing. And al-Nahr preferred their statement, saying: It is not hidden that lineage, since precaution is taken in its establishment, consideration of the time of the contract is more appropriate. His statement: 'Because we mentioned' is a cause for the refutation. His statement: 'Because you know the case' and what about if she brings a child after more than two years from the time of contract or consummation and he did not separate from her? His statement: 'And what is in Fath al-Qadir is refuted'. He said in al-Nahr: I say: Considering the beginning of the period at the time of the marriage or consummation means negating the lesser, so if she gives birth in less than a year from this beginning, his lineage is not established. And considering it from the time of separation means that if she gives birth after more than two years from the time of separation, his lineage is not established because its beginning is from the time of separation if separation occurs, and if not, then from the time of the marriage or consummation according to the difference. It is objected: if she gives birth after separation more than six months from the time of the contract or consummation and less than that from the time of separation, then his lineage is established, and the implication of what is in al-Fath is contrary. The evidence for what we have verified is that they made the period of lineage six months in the valid marriage also from the time of the contract, and it is definitely only to guard against less, not more. So also here. And Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about when the six-month period for establishing lineage (nasab) starts in a fasid (defective) marriage. The author of al-Hidayah states the position of Imam Muhammad: the period begins from consummation (al-dukhul) because a fasid marriage does not naturally lead to intercourse due to its prohibition, so mere residence (al-iqama) is considered as evidence of intercourse. This is the mufta bihi position. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize (qiyas) to a valid marriage and say the period starts from the contract. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is when a child is born six months after the contract but less than six months after consummation: according to the mufta bihi view, the child's lineage is not established. The passage also discusses the distinction between fasid and batil (void) marriage, noting that some consider marriage of mahrams batil, others fasid, and this affects the dropping of hadd. The author argues that the correct view is that hadd is dropped due to shubhah (ambiguity) of the contract. The discussion continues with a refutation of Fath al-Qadir, showing that the period of six months is only to negate the possibility of a shorter pregnancy, not to limit the maximum period of pregnancy (which is two years).

Key Terms
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikāḥ al-fāsid): A marriage contract that is defective due to missing a condition or the presence of a prohibition that can be rectified, e.g., marrying without witnesses or marrying a fifth wife while having four.
مدة النسب (muddāt al-nasab): The six-month period that must have elapsed from the start of a marriage or from possible intercourse for the child to be attributed to the husband.
الدخول (al-dukhūl): Actual sexual intercourse between spouses, as opposed to mere seclusion (khalwah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The time of the marriage contract
B) The time of consummation (dukhul)
C) The time of separation (tafriq)
D) The time of the child's birth

Key Takeaway
In a fasid marriage, the six-month lineage period begins from consummation (mufta bihi), not from the contract, due to the lack of incentive for intercourse.

The 'Idda in a Fasid Marriage: Ruling and Dispute
Ruling on 'idda in fasid marriage with dispute on its start

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on 'idda in a fasid marriage, identify the conditions for its obligation, and explain the Hanafi position on when it begins.

Core Idea
In a fasid marriage, 'idda is wajib after consummation and begins at separation, not the last intercourse.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the waiting period ('idda) in a defective (fasid) marriage. It clarifies that 'idda is obligatory only after actual intercourse (wat'), not mere seclusion (khalwah), and that it begins from the time of separation (tafriq). The author also discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the starting point, the absence of mourning (ihdad) and maintenance (nafaqa) in this 'idda, and the method of separation through either a judge's ruling or the husband's unilateral renunciation (mutaraka).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The 'idda (waiting period) in a fasid marriage. The hukm is 'wajib' (obligatory).
Wajib, not fard, due to the evidence being zanni.
2
Locate the condition for obligation
The 'idda is wajib only after actual consummation (wat'), not after khalwah (seclusion). If the couple differs about consummation, the husband's word is taken.
This is based on istihsan: assimilating the ambiguous (shubhah) to the real for caution.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the start of 'idda
There is disagreement: some (e.g., Zufar) say it begins from the last sexual act; the correct view (sahih) is that it begins from separation (tafriq).
The dalil for the correct view: the obligation arises due to shubhah and its removal by separation, similar to divorce in valid marriage.
4
Note the consequences of the 'idda
During this 'idda, the woman does not observe ihdad (mourning) and is not entitled to nafaqa (maintenance). The 'idda here is the 'idda of divorce, not death.
If the woman is the sister of the man's wife, the wife becomes haram until the 'idda ends.
5
Understand the method of separation
Separation in a fasid marriage is either by the judge's decree (tafriq al-qadi) or by the husband's unilateral renunciation (mutaraka). Mutaraka requires specific verbal formulas if the marriage was consummated.
For non-consummated marriage, some scholars hold that mere abandonment with intent suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعدة) أي وتثبت العدة فيه وجوباً بعد الوطء في النكاح الفاسد لا الخلوة. كما في القنية إلحاقاً للشبهة بالحقيقة في موضع الاحتياط، ولو اختلفا في الدخول فالقول له فلا يثبت شيء من هذه الأحكام كما في الذخيرة ولم يبين المصنف ابتداءها للاختلاف فيه والصحيح أنه من وقت التفريق لا من آخر الوطات لأنها تجب باعتبار شبهة النكاح ورفعها بالتفريق كالطلاق في النكاح الصحيح، ولا إحداد عليها في هذه العدة ولا نفقة لها فيها لأن وجوبها باعتبار الملك الثابت بالنكاح وهو منتف هنا والمراد بالعدة هنا عدة الطلاق، وأما عدة الوفاة فلا تجب عليها من النكاح الفاسد، ولو كانت هذه المرأة الموطوءة أخت امرأته حرمت عليه امرأته إلى انقضاء عدتها كذا في فتح القدير وظاهر كلامهم أن ابتداءها من وقت التفريق قضاء وديانة. وفي فتح القدير ويجب أن يكون هذا في القضاء، أما فيما بينها وبين الله تعالى إذا علمت أنها حاضت بعد آخر وطء ثلاثاً ينبغي أن يحل لها التزوج فيما بينها الله تعالى على قياس ما قدمنا من نقل العتابي ا.هـ. ومحله فيما إذا فرق بينهما، أما إذا حاضت ثلاثة حيض من آخر الوطات ولم يفارقها فليس لها التزوج اتفاقاً كما أشار إليه في غاية البيان، وظاهر كلام الزيلعي يوهم خلافه والتفريق في النكاح الفاسد إما بتفريق القاضي أو بمتاركة الزوج، ولا يتحقق الطلاق في النكاح الفاسد بل هو متاركة فيه ولا تحقق للمتاركة إلا بالقول إن كانت مدخولاً بها كقوله «تاركتك» أو «تاركتها » أو «خليت سبيلك» أو خليت سبيلها أو خليتها». وأما غير المدخول بها فتحقق المتاركة بالقول وبالترك عند بعضهم وهو تركها عل قصد أن لا يعود إليها وعند البعض لا تكون المتاركة إلا بالقول بين النسب فهي للأكثر لا للأقل فلا يرد ما ذكر فتدبر ا هـ ومثله في الرمز
His statement: (And the 'idda) i.e., the 'idda is established in it obligatorily after intercourse in the fasid marriage, not by seclusion (khalwah). As in al-Qunyah, by assimilating the ambiguous (shubhah) to the real in a place of caution. And if they differ about consummation, then the husband's word is taken, so none of these rulings are established, as in al-Dhakhirah. The author did not explain its beginning due to difference, and the correct is that it is from the time of separation, not from the last sexual act, because it becomes obligatory due to the ambiguity of the marriage and its removal by separation, like divorce in a valid marriage. There is no ihdad (mourning) for her in this 'idda, nor nafaqa (maintenance) for her in it, because its obligation is based on the ownership established by marriage, which is absent here. The intended 'idda here is the 'idda of divorce; as for the 'idda of death, it is not obligatory for her from a fasid marriage. If this woman who is cohabited is the sister of his wife, then his wife becomes unlawful for him until the conclusion of her 'idda. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the apparent meaning of their speech is that its beginning is from the time of separation judicially and religiously. In Fath al-Qadir: And this should be in judicial matters; as for between her and Allah Most High, if she knows that she has had three menses after the last intercourse, it should be permissible for her to marry between her and Allah Most High, by analogy to what we have transmitted from al-'Attabi. And its place is when there is separation between them; but if she has had three menses from the last intercourse and he has not separated from her, then it is not permissible for her to marry by agreement, as indicated in Ghayat al-Bayan. And the apparent statement of al-Zayla'i suggests otherwise. And separation in a fasid marriage is either by the judge's ruling or by the husband's abandonment (mutaraka). Divorce is not realized in a fasid marriage, rather it is mutaraka, and mutaraka is only realized by speech if she is one with whom intercourse has occurred, like his saying 'I leave you' or 'I leave her' or 'I made your way free' or 'I made her way free' or 'I left her'. As for one with whom intercourse has not occurred, mutaraka is realized by speech and, according to some, by abandonment, which is leaving her with the intention not to return to her. According to others, mutaraka is only by speech. Regarding lineage, it is for the maximum, not the minimum, so what was mentioned does not apply. Reflect. End. And similarly in al-Ramz.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage explains the 'idda (waiting period) in a fasid (defective) marriage. The ruling is that 'idda is wajib (obligatory) after actual intercourse (al-wat'), but not after mere seclusion (al-khalwah). The justification is istihsan: the ambiguous marriage is assimilated to a real one for cautiousness. The correct view is that the 'idda begins from the time of separation (al-tafriq), not from the last sexual act, because the obligation arises from the ambiguity of the marriage and its removal by separation, similar to divorce in a valid marriage. In this 'idda, the woman does not observe ihdad (mourning) nor is she entitled to nafaqa (maintenance), because maintenance in 'idda is based on ownership of the marriage, which is absent here. The 'idda here is the 'idda of divorce, not the 'idda of death (which is not applicable in fasid marriage). If the woman is the sister of the man's wife, then the wife becomes haram until the conclusion of the 'idda. The passage also discusses the difference between judicial and religious rulings regarding the end of 'idda when the woman knows she has completed three menses. Separation in fasid marriage is either by judge's decree or by the husband's unilateral renunciation (mutaraka), which requires specific verbal formulas if the marriage was consummated; for non-consummated marriage, some say mere abandonment with intent suffices.

Key Terms
العدة (al-ʿidda): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation from her husband or after his death, before she can remarry.
التفريق (al-tafrīq): Separation in a fasid marriage, achieved either by a judge's ruling (tafriq al-qadi) or by the husband's unilateral renunciation (mutaraka).
الإحداد (al-iḥdād): Mourning (refraining from adornment) observed by a widow in her 'idda of death; not required in the 'idda of a fasid marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid marriage that has been consummated, when does the 'idda begin according to the correct Hanafi view?
A) From the time of the marriage contract
B) From the time of consummation
C) From the time of separation (tafriq)
D) From the time of the last sexual act

Key Takeaway
The 'idda in a fasid marriage is wajib after consummation and begins at separation, not from the last intercourse.

Dispute Over Consequences in Fasid Marriage When Husband Denies Consummation
Ruling when spouses disagree on consummation in fasid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations from Abu Yusuf regarding the establishment of nasab, mahr, and 'idda in a fasid marriage and identify which view the matn of al-Hidayah adopts.

Core Idea
Husband's denial prevents nasab, mahr, 'idda in fasid marriage per chosen Hanafi view.

When spouses disagree about consummation in a fasid marriage, the default rule is that the husband's word is taken (al-qawlu lahu). However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: two narrations from Abu Yusuf differ on whether this denial also blocks lineage, mahr, and 'idda. This lesson walks through the dispute and shows how the matn of al-Hidayah selects one view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and default rule
The core question: if the husband denies consummation in a fasid marriage, are nasab, mahr, and 'idda established? The default rule is that the husband's word is taken (qawluh), so nothing is established.
This is based on the principle that the husband would not lie against his own interest.
2
Recall the two narrations from Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf has two narrations: (1) nasab, mahr, and 'idda are established despite the husband's denial; (2) they are not established. The second agrees with Zufar.
These narrations represent a difference in how much weight is given to the shubhah of the fasid marriage.
3
Understand Zufar's position and the matn's choice
Zufar holds that nothing is established. The matn (al-Hidayah) adopts the narration that aligns with Zufar, making it the mufta bihi view in this text.
The commentator notes that this is an 'ikhtiyar' (choice) for that narration.
4
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the chosen view: no mahr, no 'idda, no lineage. Under the other narration: mahr, 'idda, and lineage are established, even if the husband denies.
This directly affects the wife's and child's rights.
5
Consider the nuance of khalwah and the 'idda timing
The passage also mentions that if the husband did not seclude (khalwah), the child is not attributed. Additionally, there is a sub-dispute about when 'idda begins: from separation (main view) or from last sexual act (Zufar's view).
These sub-issues show the richness of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اختلفا في الدخول فالقول له فلا يثبت شيء من هذه الأحكام قال الرملي : وفي التتارخانية إذا تزوجها نكاحاً فاسداً أو خلا بها وجاءت بولد وأنكر الزوج الدخول ؛ فعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله روايتان: في رواية قال يثبت النسب ويجب المهر ،والعدة، وفي رواية لا يثبت النسب ولا يجب المهر والعدة وهو قول زفر رحمه الله ، وإن لم يخل بها لا يلزمه الولد ا.هـ. ومثله في الزيلعي فقوله «هنا لا يثبت شيء من الأحكام موافق للرواية الموافقة لقول زفر فهو اختيار لها تأمل قوله : (وظاهر الزيلعي يوهم . عبارته ويعتبر ابتداؤها من وقت التفريق وقال زفر من آخر الوطات واختاره أبو القاسم الصفار حتى لو حاضت ثلاث من آخر الوطات قبل التفريق فقد انتقضت قوله : (حتى لو تركها) قال
His statement: (And if they differ about consummation, then the husband's word is taken, so none of these rulings are established). Al-Ramli said: In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If he marries her in a fasid marriage or secludes with her, and she brings a child, and the husband denies consummation, then there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf: in one narration, lineage is established, mahr and 'idda are obligatory; in another narration, lineage is not established, nor mahr nor 'idda, and this is the statement of Zufar. And if he did not seclude with her, the child is not attributed to him. End. And similarly in al-Zayla'i, so his statement 'here nothing of these rulings is established' is in agreement with the narration that agrees with Zufar's statement, so it is his choice. Reflect. His statement: (And the apparent statement of al-Zayla'i suggests otherwise). His wording: 'And its beginning is considered from the time of separation, while Zufar said from the last sexual act, and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar chose it, so if she menstruates three times after the last intercourse before separation, then it (the 'idda) has expired.' His statement: (Even if he leaves her) he said.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This section discusses the ruling when the spouses disagree about whether consummation (dukhul) took place in a fasid marriage. The default ruling is that the husband's word is taken (qawluh), so none of the consequences (nasab, mahr, 'idda) are established. However, there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf: in one, if the husband denies and the woman brings a child, the lineage, mahr, and 'idda are still established; in the other, they are not, which agrees with Zufar. The author of al-Hidayah (the matn being commented on) seems to adopt the latter view that nothing is established. The commentary by al-Ramli and the mention of al-Zayla'i indicate that this is a matter of ikhtilaf. The passage also touches on the beginning of 'idda: Zufar holds it starts from the last sexual act, while the correct view is from separation. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar chose Zufar's view. The text ends with an incomplete sentence about 'even if he leaves her'.

Key Terms
القول له (al-qawlu lahu): The legal principle that the husband's statement is taken as true (with an oath) when he denies consummation, unless evidence contradicts.
الرواية (al-riwāyah): A transmission of a legal opinion from a Hanafi imam, especially Abu Yusuf or Muhammad al-Shaybani.
الخلا بها (khalā bihā): Seclusion with a woman in a place where intercourse could have occurred without witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The woman's word is taken
B) The husband's word is taken, so no consequences are established
C) The lineage of the child is automatically established
D) The judge decides based on evidence

Key Takeaway
In fasid marriage, the husband's denial of consummation, taken on oath, prevents establishment of nasab, mahr, and 'idda per the preferred Hanafi view.

Separation and Annulment in a Fasid Marriage
Explaining the rules of متاركة and فسخ in a fasid marriage and the fixed penalty for intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutaraka (separation) in a fasid marriage, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the woman's knowledge as a condition, and apply the rule regarding the hadd penalty for intercourse after separation.

Core Idea
In a fasid marriage, separation (mutaraka) validly dissolves the marriage; after separation, intercourse incurs the hadd penalty.

This lesson from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores how a fasid (invalid) marriage can be dissolved through mutaraka or faskh. It delves into nuanced disagreements among Hanafi scholars on who can initiate the separation and whether the woman's knowledge is required. It concludes with a critical ruling on the fixed penalty (hadd) for intercourse after the separation, distinguishing the state before and after dissolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main act and its ruling
Recognize that 'mutaraka' refers to separation in a fasid marriage. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) and dissolves the marriage.
Mutaraka is often initiated by the husband's denial of the marriage in the wife's presence.
2
Determine the two opinions on the woman's knowledge
Find the two opinions recorded in al-Qunyah: one requiring her knowledge for validity, the other (preferred) not requiring it.
The preferred view is that her knowledge is not a condition.
3
Trace the dispute on who can initiate annulment
Before consummation, both spouses can annul independently. After consummation, some require the other's presence. The woman can annul in the husband's presence by consensus.
The text shows that the woman is not excluded from initiating separation.
4
Extract the tarjih
The author prefers the second opinion (knowledge not a condition) and follows al-Zayla'i. The mufta bihi is that the woman can annul in the husband's presence.
Tarjih determines the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply the hadd penalty rule
Intercourse before separation: no hadd due to shubha. After separation: hadd is imposed because the ambiguity is removed.
The text does not explicitly distinguish between iddah and post-iddah; the ruling applies generally after separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر
استويا سناً وجمالاً ومالاً وبلداً وعصراً وعقلاً وديناً وبكارة. أن فيهما حتى لو تركها ومضى على عدتها سنون لم يكن لها أن تتزوج بآخر. وإنكار الزوج النكاح إن كان بحضرتها فهو متاركة وإلا فلا كإنكار الوكيل الوكالة، وأما علم غير المتارك بالمتاركة فنقل في القنية قولين مصححين : الأول أنه شرط لصحة المتاركة هو الصحيح حتى لو لم يعلمها لا تنقضي عدتها ثانيهما أن علم المرأة في المتاركة ليس بشرط في الأصح كما في الصحيح ا هـ . وينبغي ترجيح الثاني، ولهذا اقتصر عليه الزيلعي. وظاهر كلامهم المتاركة لا تكون من المرأة أصلاً كما قيده الزيلعي بالزوج لكن في القنية أن لكل واحد منهما أن يستبد بفسخه قبل الدخول بالإجماع وبعد الدخول مختلف فيه. وفي الذخيرة: ولكل واحد من الزوجين فسخ هذا النكاح بغير محضر من صاحبه عند بعض المشايخ . وعند بعضهم إن لم يدخل بها فكذلك وإن دخل بها فليس لواحد منهما حق الفسخ إلا بمحضر من صاحبه ا هـ . وهكذا في الخلاصة. وهذا يدل على أن للمرأة فسخه بمحضر الزوج اتفاقا»، ولا شك أن الفسخ متاركة إلا أن يفرق بينهما وهو بعيد والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. ومن أحكام العقد الفاسد أنه لا يحد بوطئها قبل التفريق للشبهة ويحد إذا وطئها بعد التفريق كذا في البدائع وغيره، وظاهره أنه لا فرق فيه بين أن يكون في العدة أو لا ولم أره صريحاً.
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr. They are equal in age, beauty, wealth, town, time, intelligence, religion, and virginity. That regarding them, even if he leaves her and years pass after her iddah, she may not marry another. And the husband's denial of the marriage: if it takes place in her presence, it is a separation (mutaraka); otherwise, it is not, like the agent's denial of agency. As for the knowledge of the one not separating about the separation, it is narrated in al-Qunyah two verified opinions: first, that it is a condition for the validity of the separation—this is sound, such that if she does not know, her iddah does not end; second, that the woman's knowledge in separation is not a condition according to the more correct view, as in al-Sahih. The second should be preferred, and for this reason al-Zayla'i restricted himself to it. The apparent meaning of their statements is that separation (mutaraka) cannot be initiated by the woman at all, as al-Zayla'i restricted it to the husband. However, in al-Qunyah, each of them may independently annul (faskh) before intercourse by consensus, and after intercourse it is disputed. In al-Dhakhira: each of the spouses may annul this marriage without the presence of the other according to some shaykhs. According to others, if he has not consummated, it is similar; but if he has consummated, then neither has the right of annulment except in the presence of the other. This indicates that the woman may annul in the presence of the husband by agreement, and there is no doubt that annulment is a separation (mutaraka), unless a distinction is made between them, which is remote. From the rulings of the invalid contract (al-`aqd al-fasid): he is not subject to the fixed penalty (hadd) for intercourse with her before separation due to ambiguity (shubha), but he is subject to hadd if he has intercourse with her after separation. This is stated in al-Bada'i` and others. Apparently there is no distinction between being in the iddah or not, and I have not seen it explicitly.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings of separation (mutaraka) and annulment (faskh) in an invalid marriage (nikah fasid). It begins by stating that if a man and woman are equal in various attributes such as age, beauty, wealth, etc., and the husband abandons her, she cannot remarry even after years because the marriage is not properly dissolved. The husband's denial of the marriage in her presence is considered a separation, otherwise not. The author then narrates from al-Qunyah two opinions regarding the woman's knowledge of the separation: one requiring it for validity, and the other (preferred) not requiring it. While some opinions restrict initiation of separation to the husband, al-Qunyah reports that each spouse can independently annul the marriage before consummation by consensus; after consummation, the permissibility is disputed. Al-Dhakhira adds that some say annulment is valid without the presence of the other party, while others require presence after consummation. The author concludes that, by consensus, the woman can annul in the husband's presence, and annulment is equivalent to separation. Finally, a ruling on the fixed penalty (hadd) for zina is stated: if one has intercourse with the woman in a fasid marriage before the separation (i.e., while the ambiguity remains), no hadd is imposed due to shubha; but if after separation, hadd is imposed. The author notes that he did not see an explicit distinction regarding whether the intercourse occurs during the iddah period or not.

Key Terms
متاركة (mutāraka): A form of separation in a fasid marriage, often initiated by the husband (or less commonly by the wife), which has the effect of dissolving the marriage.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract, which in the context of a fasid marriage can be initiated by either spouse under certain conditions.
عقد فاسد (`aqd fāsid): A marriage contract that is invalid due to a defect in its conditions or pillars, yet may produce some legal effects before annulment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No hadd is imposed due to shubha.
B) Hadd is imposed because the ambiguity has ended.
C) Hadd is imposed only if the woman was in iddah.
D) The ruling differs based on the school.

Key Takeaway
The separation (mutaraka) in a fasid marriage is valid when the husband denies the marriage in the wife's presence; the woman's knowledge is not a condition, and after separation, intercourse incurs the hadd penalty.

Determining Mahr al-Mithl: The Eight Attributes and Basis in Paternal Lineage
Detailing the eight attributes of equality for determining mahr al-mithl and additional considerations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight attributes considered for mahr al-mithl, explain the Hanafi basis in paternal relatives (qawm al-ab), and apply the ruling to determine mahr al-mithl in scenarios where the dower is unspecified.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the woman's paternal relatives and equality in eight key attributes.

When a marriage contract does not specify a valid dower, Islamic law provides a default: mahr al-mithl, the dower appropriate for a woman like her. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi approach to determining mahr al-mithl, based on the passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. You will learn the eight attributes that must be equal between the woman and her comparable peers, why the paternal lineage is the primary reference, and how additional factors like the husband's condition also play a role. Understanding this ensures fair and just dower obligations in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its evidentiary basis
The passage states that mahr al-mithl is determined by the woman's paternal relatives (qawm abiha). Note the proof: the saying of Ibn Mas'ud and the principle that a person's value is gauged by his paternal kind. Understand why maternal relatives are not considered unless they belong to the same paternal tribe.
The dalil is a Qawl Sahabi (saying of a companion), which is a secondary source in Hanafi usul.
2
List and explain the eight core attributes
The author enumerates eight attributes: age (sin), beauty (jamal), wealth (mal), town (balad), time/era (asr), intelligence (aql), religion (din), and virginity (bakara). For each, understand how they affect the dower. Note that some scholars add knowledge, manners, character, and childlessness.
The text notes that for families of high status, beauty is not the sole criterion; for middle-class people, it is more relevant.
3
Consider the husband's attributes
The passage extends the analysis to the husband: he should be comparable to husbands of the woman's peers in wealth, status, beauty, locale, piety, etc. This is based on the idea that a young man may marry an older woman, and a pious man may command a lower dower.
The author follows Fath al-Qadir in considering the husband's attributes, but some earlier shaykhs also add this.
4
Distinguish between free and slave women
For free women, the full set of attributes applies. For slave women, the dower is determined by market demand or, according to al-Awza'i, a fixed proportion (one-third for virgins, one-sixth for non-virgins). This distinction is crucial because the ruling's scope changes.
The text cites Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Mujtaba for the rule on slave women.
5
Apply the ruling to marriage types
Mahr al-mithl applies in valid marriages where the dower is unspecified, unknown, or invalid, and in fasid (defective) marriages after consummation. For intercourse under shubha (ambiguity), a different calculation may be used.
The passage clarifies that the mahr al-mithl discussed here is not for shubha cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومهر مثلها يعتبر بقوم أبيها إذا استويا سناً وجمالاً ومالاً وبلداً وعصراً وعقلاً وديناً وبكارة) بيان لشيئين: أحدهما أن الاعتبار لقوم الأب في مهر المثل لقول ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه لها مهر مثل المذكورة لأن المهر يختلف باختلاف هذه الأوصاف. وكذا يختلف باختلاف الدار والعصر أي الزمان وقد ذكر المصنف ثمانية أشياء. وأراد بالسن الصغر أو الكبر، وأطلق في اعتبار الجمال والمال، وقيل لا يعتبر في بيت الحسب والشرف وإنما يعتبر ذلك في أوساط الناس إذ الرغبة فيهن للجمال بخلاف بيت الشرف. وفي فتح القدير: وهذا جيدا هـ. والظاهر اعتباره مطلقاً. وأراد بالدين التقوى كما ذكره العيني وزاد في التبيين على هذه الثمانية أربعة وهي: العلم والأدب وكمال الخلق وأن لا يكون لها ولد . وزاد المشايخ بأنه يعتبر حال الزوج أيضاً. وفسره في فتح القدير بأن يكون زوج هذه كأزواج أمثالها من نسائها في المال والحسب وعدمهما ا هـ. وينبغي أن لا يختص بهذين الشيئين لأن للجمال والبلد والعصر والعقل والتقوى والسن مدخلاً من جهة الزوج أيضاً فينبغي اعتبارها في حقه أيضاً لأن الشاب يتزوج الشيخ، وكذا المتقي بأرخص من الفاسق . وأشار بقوله ما لا إلى أن الكلام إنما هو في الحرة ولذا قال في شرح الطحاوي والمجتبى : مهر مثل الأمة على قدر الرغبة فيها. وعن الأوزاعي : : ثلث قيمتها. ثم اعلم أن اعتبار مهر المثل بما ذكر حكم كل نكاح صحيح تسمية فيه أصلاً أو فيه ما هو مجهول أو ما لا يحل شرعاً كما قدمنا تفاصيله، وحكم كل نكاح فاسد بعد الوطء سمى فيه مهر أو لا، وأما المواضع التي يجب فيها المهر بسبب الوطء بشبهة فليس المراد بالمهر فيها مهر المثل المذكور هنا لما في الخلاصة بعد ذكر المواضع سمی بأرخص من تفويض فلا يدل ما نقله على صحة متاركتها فتدبر قوله : (ولم أره صريحاً) سيذكر المؤلف في باب العدة أنه ينبغي أن يقيد بما بعد العدة لأن وطء المعتدة لا يوجب الحد اهـ. وأقره عليه في النهر هناك وسيأتي رده قوله : (والظاهر اعتباره مطلقاً) وكذا قال في النهر، وإطلاق الكتاب كغيره يرده قوله : (فينبغي اعتبارها في حقه أيضاً وافقه على هذا البحث في النهر ما في الخلاصة وقال بعض المحققين : العقر في الحرائر مهر المثل، وفي الجواري إذا كن أبكاراً عشر القيمة، وإن كن ثيبات نصف العشر، وقيل في الجواري ينظر إلى مثل تلك الجارية جمالاً ومولى بكم تتزوج
His saying: (And her dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) is considered based on her father's people (qawm abiha) when they are equal in age, beauty, wealth, town, time, intelligence, religion, and virginity.) An explanation of two things: First, that the consideration is for the father's people in the mahr al-mithl, due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'She has the dower of the like of her womenfolk, and they are the paternal relatives,' and because a person is from the kind of his father's people, and the value of a thing is only known by considering the value of its kind; it is not considered by her mother or aunt if they are not from her tribe. Second, that equality in the mentioned attributes is necessary because the dower varies with these attributes. Similarly, it varies with the dwelling and time (i.e., the era). The author mentioned eight things. He intended by age (sin) young or old; he left the consideration of beauty and wealth unrestricted; it is said that for families of status and honor, it is not considered, but for middle-class people it is, as desire in them is for beauty, unlike families of honor. In Fath al-Qadir: This is good. The apparent view is to consider it absolutely. He intended by religion (din) piety, as mentioned by al-Ayni. In al-Tabyin, four more were added to these eight: knowledge, etiquette, completeness of character, and that she have no child. The shaykhs added that the condition of the husband is also considered. In Fath al-Qadir, he explains that her husband should be like the husbands of her peers among her womenfolk in wealth and status and their absence. It should not be restricted to these two things, because beauty, dwelling, time, intelligence, piety, and age also have a bearing from the husband's side, so they should be considered in his case as well, because a young man marries an old woman, and similarly a pious man is cheaper than a sinful one. His saying 'ma la' indicates that the discussion is only about the free woman; thus it is said in Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Mujtaba: the mahr of a slave woman is according to the desire for her. From al-Awza'i: one third of her value. Then know that the consideration of mahr al-mithl as mentioned is the ruling for every valid marriage where a dower is named in the original or where it is unknown or something legally impermissible, as we have detailed previously, and for every fasid marriage after consummation, whether a dower is named or not. As for the cases where dower is obligatory due to intercourse under ambiguity (shubha), the intended dower there is not the mahr al-mithl mentioned here, as in al-Khulasa after mentioning the cases it was called cheaper than? ... it does not indicate the validity of her mutaraka. Then he said: His saying: (And I have not seen it explicitly) will be mentioned by the author in the chapter of iddah that it should be restricted to after the iddah, because intercourse with a woman in iddah does not obligate hadd. He agreed with this in al-Nahr, and later he will refute it. His saying: (The apparent view is to consider it absolutely) is also said in al-Nahr, and the unrestricted nature of the book refutes it. His saying: (It should be considered in his case too) he agreed with this research in al-Nahr and al-Ramz. His saying: (Due to what is in al-Khulasa) he mentioned what is in al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and Ghurar al-Afkar, and similarly al-Maqdisi mentioned it in al-Ramz, then said: In Waqi`at al-Natafi: the mahr al-mithl is what a woman like her marries for. I say: In al-Fayd by al-Kurki after mentioning the gist of al-Khulasa, some investigators said: The `aqr (dower) for free women is mahr al-mithl, for slave women if they are virgins it is one-tenth of the value, if non-virgins one-twentieth, and it is said for slave women one looks at a like of that slave woman in beauty and her master for how much she marries.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This section from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rules for determining the mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) when a proper dower is not specified. The author comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq which states that the mahr al-mithl is based on the woman's paternal relatives (qawm abiha), provided the spouses are equal in eight attributes: age, beauty, wealth, town, time (era), intelligence, religion, and virginity. He clarifies two main points: First, the basis is the father's family, proven by the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) and by the rational principle that a person's value is measured by his paternal lineage. The mother's or aunt's side is not considered unless they belong to the same tribe. Second, equality in all mentioned attributes is necessary because the dower varies with each. The author notes that time and place also affect the value. He mentions that some scholars add four more attributes: knowledge, manners, perfect character, and childlessness. Others add the husband's condition: he should be comparable to husbands of her peers. The author advises that the husband's attributes like beauty, locale, and piety should also be considered, as they affect the dower. He then distinguishes between free and slave women: for free women, the rules above apply; for slaves, the mahr is based on demand or, according to al-Awza'i, a fraction of her value. Finally, he notes that the mahr al-mithl is applicable in valid marriages where the dower is unspecified, unknown, or invalid, and in fasid marriages after consummation. For cases of dower due to shubha, a different calculation may apply.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower that is appropriate for a woman like her, determined by her comparable peers (aqrab) with consideration of various attributes.
قوم الأب (qawm al-ab): The paternal relatives of the woman, specifically her father's family and tribe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the eight core attributes for determining mahr al-mithl?
A) Age (sin)
B) Beauty (jamal)
C) Knowledge ('ilm)
D) Virginity (bakara)

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is determined by a woman's paternal relatives with equality in eight attributes, and the husband's condition also affects the amount.

Mahr al-Mithl: Eight Criteria and the Proof from Paternal Relatives
Expansion on the eight criteria for mahr al-mithl based on paternal relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight criteria for mahr al-mithl and explain why the Hanafi school relies on the paternal relatives for its assessment.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl is benchmarked by the bride's paternal female relatives, not her maternal side.

When no dower is fixed or the specified dower is invalid, Islamic law requires a proper dower (mahr al-mithl). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi criteria for determining that amount, based on the commentary of Ibn Nujaym. You will learn the eight attributes that must be equal between the bride and her comparable relatives, and the key proof from the Companion Ibn Mas'ud that anchors the assessment to the father's lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
Read the opening: مهر مثلها يعتبر بقوم أبيها. Recognize that the ruling is: mahr al-mithl is assessed by the women of the father's side. Note the proof: Ibn Mas'ud's statement 'لها مهر مثل نسائها' and the principle that a person's value is known by its kind.
The proof is a Qawl Sahabi (saying of a Companion), which Hanafis accept as a source.
2
List the Eight Attributes
From the text, extract the eight attributes: age, beauty, wealth, city, time/era, intelligence, religion (piety), and virginity. Understand that these affect the dower amount.
The author (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) mentions exactly eight; the commentator elaborates.
3
Analyze the Additional Criteria
Note the four additions from al-Tabyin (knowledge, refinement, perfect character, no child) and the mashayikh's addition of the husband's condition. Consider whether these are included in the mufta bihi view.
The commentator suggests the husband's condition should not be limited to wealth and lineage but includes all eight attributes.
4
Distinguish Between Free and Slave Women
The passage ends with a note that the discussion is for free women. For slave women, mahr al-mithl is based on demand or one-third of value. This is an important exception.
This distinction comes from Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Mujtaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومهر مثلها يعتبر بقوم أبيها إذا استويا سناً وجمالاً ومالاً وبلداً وعصراً وعقلاً وديناً وبكارة) بيان لشيئين: أحدهما أن الاعتبار لقوم الأب في مهر المثل لقول ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه لها مهر مثل نسائها وهن أقارب الأب، ولأن الإنسان من جنس قوم أبيه وقيمة الشيء إنما تعرف بالنظر في قيمة جنسه ولا يعتبر بأمها وخالتها، إذا لم يكونا من قبيلتها لما بينا . ثانيهما أنه لا بد من الاستواء في الأوصاف المذكورة لأن المهر يختلف باختلاف هذه الأوصاف. وكذا يختلف باختلاف الدار والعصر أي الزمان وقد ذكر المصنف ثمانية أشياء. وأراد بالسن الصغر أو الكبر، وأطلق في اعتبار الجمال والمال، وقيل لا يعتبر في بيت الحسب والشرف وإنما يعتبر ذلك في أوساط الناس إذ الرغبة فيهن للجمال بخلاف بيت الشرف. وفي فتح القدير: وهذا جيدا هـ. والظاهر اعتباره مطلقاً. وأراد بالدين التقوى كما ذكره العيني وزاد في التبيين على هذه الثمانية أربعة وهي: العلم والأدب وكمال الخلق وأن لا يكون لها ولد . وزاد المشايخ بأنه يعتبر حال الزوج أيضاً. وفسره في فتح القدير بأن يكون زوج هذه كأزواج أمثالها من نسائها في المال والحسب وعدمهما ا هـ. وينبغي أن لا يختص بهذين الشيئين لأن للجمال والبلد والعصر والعقل والتقوى والسن مدخلاً من جهة الزوج أيضاً فينبغي اعتبارها في حقه أيضاً لأن الشاب يتزوج الشيخ، وكذا المتقي بأرخص من الفاسق . وأشار بقوله ما لا إلى أن الكلام إنما هو في الحرة ولذا قال في شرح الطحاوي والمجتبى : مهر مثل الأمة على قدر الرغبة فيها. وعن الأوزاعي : : ثلث قيمتها.
His statement: (And her mahr al-mithl is considered by the women of her father, if they are equal in age, beauty, wealth, city, time, intelligence, religion, and virginity) is an explanation of two things: First, that consideration is given to the women of the father in mahr al-mithl because of the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him: 'For her is the mahr of her female relatives,' and they are the relatives of the father, and because a person is of the lineage of his father's people, and the value of a thing is only known by looking at the value of its kind, and no consideration is given to her mother and maternal aunt if they are not from her tribe, as we have explained. Second, that equality in the mentioned attributes is necessary because the mahr differs with the difference of these attributes. Likewise, it differs with the difference of residence and time, i.e., the era, and the author mentioned eight things. He intended by 'age' youth or old age, and he left the consideration of beauty and wealth open. It is said that it is not considered in a house of lineage and honor, but rather that is considered among the middle class of people, for desire for them is for beauty, unlike a house of honor. In Fath al-Qadir: 'This is good.' And the apparent view is to consider it absolutely. He intended by 'religion' piety as mentioned by al-Ayni, and in al-Tabyin he added four more to these eight: knowledge, refinement, perfection of character, and that she should not have a child. The mashayikh added that the husband's condition is also considered. In Fath al-Qadir it is explained that the husband of this woman should be like the husbands of her female counterparts in wealth and lineage or lack thereof. And it is appropriate that it should not be limited to these two things, because beauty, city, time, intelligence, piety, and age also have a bearing from the husband's side, so they should be considered for him as well, for a young man marries an old woman, and likewise a pious man is cheaper than a sinful one. He indicated by his statement 'what not' that the discussion is only about a free woman, hence it is said in Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Mujtaba: The mahr al-mithl of a slave woman is according to the desire for her. And from al-Awza'i: one-third of her value.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling on mahr al-mithl. The commentator explains that mahr al-mithl is assessed by looking at the women of the father's side (paternal relatives), not the mother's side, because the Prophet's companion Ibn Mas'ud said the mahr is like that of her female relatives (paternal cousins, aunts, etc.). This is supported by the principle that a person's value is known by similar kind. The author then lists eight essential attributes: age (youth/old age), beauty, wealth, city, time (era), intelligence, religion (piety), and virginity. Equality in these is required because the mahr varies with them. Some scholars add four more: knowledge, refinement, perfect character, and not having a child. The mashayikh also consider the husband's condition, meaning the mahr should be similar to what husbands of comparable women give. The commentator notes that these criteria are for free women; for slave women, mahr al-mithl is based on demand or a fixed fraction (one-third of value per al-Awza'i).

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the dower of comparable women when no specific dower is fixed or is invalid.
قوم الأب (qawm al-ab): The paternal relatives of the bride, whose mahr is used as a benchmark.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The Quranic verse on mahr
C) The saying of Ibn Mas'ud
D) Analogy (qiyas) from the value of goods

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is assessed by the bride's paternal female relatives, and the eight criteria ensure a fair comparison.

The Definition and Application of 'Uqr in Hanafi Fiqh
Distinction between mahr al-mithl and 'uqr with procedural details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mahr al-mithl and 'uqr, state the mufta bihi definition of 'uqr, and apply the procedural rules for determining mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, 'uqr for shubha intercourse equals mahr al-mithl according to the relied-upon view.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the rules for mahr al-mithl apply to valid and invalid marriages, but for intercourse under a shubha (mistaken belief), the dower is called 'uqr. The definition of 'uqr is contested within the Hanafi school, with some equating it to mahr al-mithl and others to a hiring-for-zina valuation. The text resolves this by citing Abu Hanifa's authoritative narration and also discusses procedural requirements such as witness testimony and the judge's role in fixing mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three contexts for dower obligation
The passage distinguishes between valid marriage (mahr al-mithl if no mahr or invalid specification), invalid marriage after intercourse (mahr al-mithl), and shubha intercourse ('uqr).
Focus on the shift from mahr al-mithl to 'uqr.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'uqr
Two definitions are presented: (1) The amount one would hire for zina (from al-Khulasah and some scholars), and (2) Mahr al-mithl (from Abu Hanifa via al-Hujjah).
Note the citation of al-Hujjah as a source of zahir al-riwayah.
3
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'wa 'alayhi al-fatwa' after quoting Abu Hanifa, indicating that 'uqr is mahr al-mithl is the relied-upon position.
4
Examine the procedural rules for mahr al-mithl
The passage discusses who testifies, the role of witnesses (two men or one man and two women), and the judge's authority to fix mahr al-mithl. It also mentions that mutual agreement of the spouses overrides strict criteria.
Note the contradiction between al-Muhit and other sources regarding the judge's role.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical scenario
Synthesize: if a woman has intercourse under a shubha, the husband owes mahr al-mithl, not a hiring-based amount.
This is the practical consequence of the mufta bihi view.

فيها المهر بسبب الوطء بشبهة فليس المراد بالمهر فيها مهر المثل المذكور هنا لما في الخلاصة بعد ذكر المواضع التي يجب فيها المهر بالوطء عن شبهة قال : والمراد من المهر العقر وتفسير العقر الواجب بالوطء في فالزيادة على مهر المثل عند إبائه والنقص عنه عند إبائها لا يجوز اهـ. قلت لكن في القهستاني ما يؤيد كلام المؤلف حيث قال : وهذا كله إذا لم يفرض القاضي في مهر المثل شيئاً ولم يتراض الزوجان على شيء منه وإلا Then know that the consideration of mahr al-mithl as mentioned is the ruling for every valid marriage with a specification originally, or where there is something unknown or legally impermissible as we have detailed before, and the ruling for every invalid marriage after intercourse whether a mahr was named or not. As for the contexts where mahr is obligatory due to intercourse under a shubha (mistaken belief), the intended mahr there is not the mahr al-mithl mentioned here because in al-Khulasah after mentioning the contexts where mahr is obligatory due to intercourse under shubha, it says: 'The intended meaning of mahr is al-‘uqr, and the interpretation of the obligatory ‘uqr for intercourse in some contexts is what Shaykh Najm al-Din said: I asked the Qadi Imam al-Asbijabi about that for a fatwa, and he wrote: It is al-‘uqr, and it is considered by how much one would hire for zina if it were lawful; that amount is obligatory.' And similarly transmitted from our mashayikh in Sharh al-Asl by Imam al-Sarakhsi. Its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between a free woman and a slave woman, but it contradicts what is in al-Muhit: 'If a woman is sent to him as a bride other than his wife and he has intercourse with her, he owes her mahr al-mithl.' Unless it is interpreted as the 'uqr mentioned in al-Khulasah for reconciliation. I have not seen a ruling if a woman is equal to two women from her father's relatives in all considered attributes but their mahrs differ in amount, whether the lesser or greater mahr is considered. It is appropriate that any mahr that the judge considers and rules upon is valid due to minor variance. In al-Khulasah: 'He is considered by his sisters, paternal aunts, and their daughters; if he has no sister or paternal aunt, then by the daughter of the paternal sister and the daughter of the paternal uncle.' Its apparent meaning is that the daughter of the paternal sister and daughter of the paternal uncle are deferred, so it follows that if he has a sister and a paternal uncle's daughter equal in the mentioned attributes, the paternal uncle's daughter is not considered in the presence of the sister, but the apparent meaning of their statements contradicts that. In al-Khulasah: 'It is required that the one informing about mahr al-mithl be two men or one man and two women, and the wording of testimony is required. If there are no just witnesses for that, then the statement of the husband with his oath is accepted.' Its apparent meaning is that mahr al-mithl is not adjudicated without testimony, or the husband's acknowledgment is valid. But what is in al-Muhit contradicts: 'If the judge or the husband after the affliction fixates, it is valid, and it is considered thereby, and that is the chosen opinion.' In the twelfth chapter of al-Tatarkhaniyyah in one type concerning the obligation of mahr without marriage, it mentions what is here attributed to al-Muhit, then adds: 'In al-Hujjah, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa: The interpretation of ‘uqr is what a woman of her like marries for, and upon that is the fatwa.' So it is clear that there is a difference in the matter, and the mufta bihi is contrary to what is here. His statement: 'And it contradicts what is in al-Muhit' was not mentioned because of what passed from al-Khaniyyah: If a man marries a prohibited woman, there is no hadd in the view of Abu Hanifa, and he owes her mahr al-mithl whatever it reaches, because here the intended is intercourse under shubha without marriage, as evidence by his statement before: 'And the ruling of every invalid marriage' and the case of al-Khaniyyah is of that type, not of what we are discussing. And with what we have established, what was said that it also contradicts the author's earlier statement 'and he did not increase over the named amount' is repelled. His statement: 'And it is appropriate that any mahr that the judge considers...' Al-Ramli said: 'Our scholars have stated that entrusting to the judges of the era is corruption, and what the juristic consideration requires is considering the lesser for certainty, so that the husband's liability is not occupied with other than it. Ponder.' I say: It appears to me that one looks at the mahr of each of these two women; whose mahr matches the mahr of her equals is considered, for it is possible that in the mahr of one there was favoritism from the husband or the wife. Ponder. His statement: 'And it contradicts what is in al-Muhit' was answered by al-Nahr that what is in al-Muhit should be interpreted as when they both agree to that; otherwise, increasing above mahr al-mithl when he refuses or decreasing when she refuses is not permissible. I say: But in al-Qahistani there is support for the author's statement where he said: 'All this is if the judge did not fix something for mahr al-mithl nor did the spouses mutually agree on something, otherwise it is the mahr as in al-Mashari‘.' So his statement 'and they did not mutually agree' indicates that the ruling is not by their mutual agreement, and the matter was also mentioned by al-Hakim al-Shahid in...
